Current Affairs Commentary

The Call for Abolishing Exorbitant Taxes and Miscellaneous Levies (England)

Recently, President Wang of the Executive Yuan, in his capacity as Chairman of the Rural Reconstruction Commission of the Executive Yuan, telegraphed all provinces, cities, counties, and people's organizations across the country, requesting detailed reports on the names and amounts of various taxes and levies in their respective localities. This was to facilitate collation, verification, and the convening of relevant agencies to discuss methods for abolishing and streamlining them, thereby alleviating the people's hardships and gradually enriching their livelihoods. At a time when the nation is facing economic decline and both internal and external troubles are pressing, it is gratifying that the government authorities are aware of the root causes of the people's suffering and are seeking to abolish these most disruptive exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous levies. It is said that the policy of abolishing exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous levies is a vital national plan of our government. The government has previously promulgated clear orders for implementation. Later, before the purification of the party, a committee for improving taxes and levies was established. The order to abolish exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous levies in Shandong upon completion of this task shows that the government's intention to start anew with the people did not begin today. However, in recent years, the exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous levies throughout the country have become even more numerous and disruptive than before the fifteenth year of the Republic. Is this due to difficulties in implementation, or to ineffective enforcement of orders by those responsible? Or is it due to the country's frequent troubles and repeated internal strife, leaving no time for this? Some argue that today, our country's mountains and rivers are fragmented, society is unstable, and both urban and rural areas lack vitality. The biggest problem is the invasion of foreign economic forces. Therefore, if the government authorities sincerely want to save the people's livelihood, they should first focus on this. However, I believe that abolishing these exorbitant and miscellaneous taxes is precisely to increase our people's ability to resist the invasion of foreign forces. Therefore, the abolition of exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous levies should be implemented swiftly with a firm and sincere attitude. If it must first be preceded by a detailed investigation, followed by streamlining and verification, and then convening meetings for leisurely discussion, I fear that delays will lead to disappointment and turn it into a bubble.

Today's so-called exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous levies have tax names and goods classifications that vary widely from place to place. There are taxes on bamboo and wood, and taxes on chickens and ducks. The tax-collecting agencies are often layered upon layered. The province collects, the county government collects, the town market collects, and the stationed troops also collect. The extent of the burden on the people can be said to have reached its limit. It is imperative to conduct a very detailed investigation. However, the ultimate burden of these taxes, in reality, mostly falls on the general poor and helpless common people across the country, while the few wealthy individuals in urban and rural areas remain unaffected. The taxpayer is the consumer himself, of course. However, most of the taxpayers are merchants engaged in buying and selling, factory owners who purchase raw materials, and wealthy people who manage land. In fact, they can all pass on the entire amount of the taxes they pay to the consumers. And the general consumers have no choice but to swallow their anger and let them exploit them. Even if the merchants and the wealthy cannot raise prices excessively, they rarely suffer losses. Even if the burden of exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous levies hinders their business development, it is still a secondary issue among the various socio-economic problems today. Therefore, the harm of exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous levies to society and the people is so great, how can the abolition be delayed? Now the authorities are advocating a fresh start with the people, and do not hesitate to speak out about reform because the exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous levies are important sources of revenue for the local authorities. It cannot be said that it is not the good fortune of the common people. It is hoped that the government authorities can muster their courage and accomplish this with all their strength. Do not just offer empty words of kindness, and remain like the past, leaving future generations to reminisce. Then it may be possible.

Farmers' Associations in Various Districts of Beijing City Aid Detained Farmers

(Nanjing) The Farmers' Associations in various districts of Beijing City, in order to aid the detained farmers of Xiaohuangzhou, held a second emergency meeting on the afternoon of the 29th, and then braved the rain to petition the Central Party Headquarters, personally submitting a petition demanding: (1) Removal and punishment of the Mayor; (2) Please order the Municipal Government to declare its acceptance of the following matters within three days; (3) Representatives of the Municipal Government and various district Farmers' Associations shall go to the court to release the eight detained representatives; (4) Allocate land for cultivation without violating the regulations of the Executive Yuan, in order to enable farmers to have their own land; (5) The Municipal Government shall provide travel expenses to the forty-four detained individuals to return to the island for cultivation. The liaison department dispatched personnel to meet with them, promising to submit the petition to the Secretary-General for handling. The six district party headquarters of Beijing City resolved to aid the farmers of Xiaohuangzhou: (1) Present a petition to the Municipal Party Headquarters, and send a letter to the Municipal Government ordering the immediate release of the arrested farmers; (2) Present a petition to the Municipal Party Headquarters, together with the Municipal Government, to quickly raise relief measures; (3) Present a petition to the Municipal Party Headquarters to be forwarded to the Central Government, to severely investigate the Mayor. (29th Dispatch)

Chen Shaokuan Submits a Request to the Executive Yuan for Commendation and Compensation for Du Xigui

(Nanjing) Naval Commander Chen Shaokuan, considering that Du Xigui had made many contributions to the Navy, and had recently achieved remarkable results in managing the Naval Academy, plans to hold a memorial service in Beijing in January of next year. Furthermore, considering Du's many years of service in the Navy and his contributions to the party and the country, he has specially requested the Executive Yuan to forward the request to the National Government for an official commendation and preferential treatment. The provisional meeting of the Executive Yuan on the 29th has already approved it. (29th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Du Xigui, styled Shencheng, was 60 years old and from Minhou, Fujian. He graduated from the Qing Dynasty Nanjing Naval Academy. After the establishment of the Republic of China, he successively served as the commander of the Chen-class torpedo boat and the Jiangzhen gunboat of the Naval Guard. In the sixth year of the Republic, he served as the commander of the Second Fleet of the Navy. In the eleventh year, he served as the Commander-in-Chief of the Navy. In the thirteenth year, when Huang Fu formed the cabinet, Du served as the Minister of the Navy. In the fifteenth year, he concurrently served as the Acting Prime Minister of the State Council. After the establishment of the National Government, Du was specially appointed as the commissioner to inspect the navies of European and American countries. In the twentieth year, after returning to China, he successively served as the principal of the Mawei Naval Academy. Du had one wife and one concubine, who are currently residing in Shanghai. He had two sons. The elder son, named Yisi, studied dentistry in the United States. After returning to China the previous year, he worked at the Le Coal Mining Company in Tianjin. The younger son is currently studying navigation in the Navy and accompanied his father to Beijing last month. After receiving telegrams of condolence from their families, both sons left for Shanghai to attend the funeral one after another the day before yesterday. (29th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Admiral Du Xigui, principal of the Mawei Naval Academy in Fujian, passed away suddenly at his residence in Shanghai at 2:00 PM on the 27th of this month due to a relapse of pneumonia. After receiving the news, the naval department immediately ordered all ships and agencies under its jurisdiction to fly flags at half-mast for three days starting from the 29th to express mourning. Furthermore, according to a responsible person of the naval department speaking to reporters, the naval academy's affairs will continue as usual after Du's death. The naval department is currently vying to find a successor for the position of principal. (29th Central News Agency Dispatch)

East and West Face Each Other from Afar

Important Diplomatic Speeches by American and Russian Leaders

Both Call for Peace

Roosevelt Declares No Ambition to Covet the Territory of Other Countries

Molotov Expresses Willingness to Be Friendly to Japan, But Must Be Wary

Roosevelt's New Declaration

Holds No Ambition to Expand Territory

Opposes Any Military Intervention

Willing to Work with the League of Nations

To Promote the Welfare of the World's Nations

(Washington) Today is the birthday of former President Wilson. President Roosevelt delivered an important speech on American diplomacy at the board meeting of the "Wilson Foundation," stating that the United States will never invade the land of others in the future, and opposes any interference in the affairs of Latin American countries. He then praised the achievements of Secretary of State Hull at the Pan-American Conference, saying that wars are caused by the rulers of countries, not by the people. Former President Wilson made many efforts to promote mutual understanding among the nations of the world. Wilson once declared that the United States no longer coveted an inch of the territory of other countries. The United States has regarded this declaration as a guiding principle. Wilson's declaration was even more important when he expressed his views to the Latin American countries, saying that human freedom should not be exploited for material interests. It is a pity that this frank policy failed to achieve its full effect due to the impact of the European War. Today, I dare to issue a new declaration in addition to Wilson's declaration in my capacity as President, stating that the United States' policy opposes any military intervention in the future. "The constitutional government of other countries must be maintained. The United States does not bear the obligation. If chaos occurs in other countries on the American continent, its impact will affect the entire continent, not just one country." The reason why the Pan-American Conference in the capital of Uruguay was so successful is that the countries of the Americas were able to understand this theory, and not only the authorities of each country, but also the people of each country deeply understood this meaning. At this time, the thinking of the nations of the Americas is very good. Shortsighted people believe that Wilson's plans have failed. This erroneous view originates from the national ideas of the people, but the blame for threatening peace should be attributed to the authorities of each country, not to the people of each country. Roosevelt continued, "Wilson's call to the world to abolish war was met with joy by the people of all countries. However, the politicians, or self-proclaimed politicians, who gathered in Paris in 1919 to negotiate the peace treaty mostly regarded Wilson's application as a mere formality, focusing on national political interests, personal prestige, and national expansion. The League of Nations was born in this bad atmosphere. Fortunately, the League of Nations has made many contributions since its establishment. When countries encounter disputes, they all directly or indirectly rely on it to seek better solutions. Most diplomatic negotiations are given the opportunity to proceed by the League of Nations. The League of Nations has also made efforts in formulating plans for health, commerce, education, and other undertakings. Large and small countries rely on it to resolve disputes, regardless of size. The United States is cooperating with the League of Nations openly, more so now than at any other time. The League of Nations is the mainstay of world peace. Although the United States is not a member country and does not want to join the League of Nations, the United States will fully cooperate with its efforts to protect the lives and promote the welfare of all nations of the world." Roosevelt then said that 10% of the people in the world threaten others and are feared by the other 90%. Roosevelt also recalled the various proposals made by the League of Nations to the world, among which universal disarmament and the abandonment of armed aggression were the most important. He concluded, "All these benevolent proposals have unfortunately failed. The political leaders of various countries gathered in Geneva justified their mistakes with ridiculous reasons. Although these people speak in the name of the people, they are not enough to represent the people. I dare to say to these people that if the people of the world can speak directly, then the agreement to jointly maintain peace in the world can be concluded immediately. The war of 1914 and the wars in history before that were all caused by the governments of various countries and had nothing to do with the people. We dare to use Wilson's words to tell the world. What are his words? That is, from now on, the rulers of various countries are not allowed to cause wars, but the people of various countries are allowed to establish peace themselves." (28th Havas Dispatch)

Good Impression in Cuba

Havana Yesterday was the birthday of the late President Wilson. President Roosevelt delivered a speech, repeatedly reiterating the policy of non-interference in the affairs of other countries. This speech has had a warm impression on the Cuban government. President Samartan recently issued a declaration praising Roosevelt, saying that the Cuban government and people fully agree with President Roosevelt's statement that "armed intervention is the root of disputes and can cause countries to compete with each other." (29th Havas Dispatch)

Molotov Explains the International Position of Soviet Russia

Firmly Declares that Soviet Russia Aims at Peace

But is Also Prepared to Cope with the Danger of Being Attacked

(Moscow) The Central Executive Committee of the Soviet Union met yesterday. People's Commissar Chairman Molotov reported on the plan for developing the Soviet Union's national economy in 1934 to enthusiastic applause. At the end of the report, Molotov discussed the Soviet Union's international position, saying,

The Greatest Success of US-Russia Hand-in-Hand Diplomacy

"The year 1933 was a year in which the Soviet Union's international position was further consolidated. The facts have already stated this for themselves. The resumption of diplomatic relations between the Soviet Union and the United States was the greatest success of the Soviet Union's foreign policy. The motivation for this came from Roosevelt. This is well known. The Soviet government immediately accepted this motivation. Thus, the artificial obstacles to diplomatic relations between the two largest countries (we cannot blame anyone for the existence of these obstacles) were finally eliminated. And the warm welcome given by the American people to Litvinov has shown to what extent this resumption of diplomatic relations has satisfied the essential requirements and deep desires of the Soviet Union and the United States. The establishment of diplomatic relations between the Soviet Union and the United States is based on an agreement. This agreement is fully in line with the principles of the Soviet Union's foreign policy. Now that diplomatic relations have been established, the development of trade and economic relations will be able to proceed more smoothly."

The Center of Policy is to Strive for Peace

Molotov stressed, "Under the current international situation, it is particularly important that the establishment of this relationship will have a huge and beneficial impact on the stability of international relations and the consolidation of world peace. In this regard, we must recognize that the Soviet government's resolutely implemented foreign policy has achieved important successes. The issue of fighting for world peace in the past and present is also the center of our attention. This struggle to win peace and the struggle against the rising tide of imperialist war will be able to accommodate not only the deepest wishes of the Soviet Union but also the deepest wishes of the people of other countries. We have no doubt about this. The Soviet government is strengthening its struggle for peace in various ways as the elements promoting the rising tide of imperialist war are increasing in international relations, as this situation is driven by the frantic increase in armaments and military budgets, and as the work of preparing for a new war is being carried out in many places before everyone's eyes, regardless of the fact that the ruling groups of some countries are promoting their aggressive attempts."

No Worries in the West, Mutually Concluded Non-Aggression Pacts

Molotov continued, "Soviet diplomacy has achieved important victories this year. Soviet diplomacy has gloriously completed the following tasks, namely, openly and resolutely exposing aggressive imperialist forces, opposing them with clear proposals, and denouncing their attempts to resolve international disputes by armed force. Everyone should recall that the disarmament conference's delay in resolving this issue did not prevent us from concluding a pact defining aggressor countries with several neighboring countries, namely Poland, Finland, Estonia, Latvia, Lithuania, Romania, Czechoslovakia, Turkey, Persia, and Afghanistan. These victories of Soviet diplomacy are inextricably linked to Litvinov's fame. His achievements are well known to the general public, but I must specifically state them here (long applause). I expect that the entire audience will welcome the following suggestion, namely, that Litvinov should make a more detailed report on this issue of international government (applause)."

Maintaining Friendship and Cooperation with Italy, France, Poland, and Turkey

Molotov continued, "In its relations with other countries, the Soviet government has resolutely implemented its tested principles of peace and its policy of practical cooperation. The clearest example of this is our relationship with Turkey. During Turkey's tenth anniversary, the Soviet government sent a delegation headed by Voroshilov to Turkey. At the same time, this friendly country gave the delegation a very warm welcome. These facts are sufficient to demonstrate the stability of Soviet-Turkish relations and its political significance. At this time, I should mention that the development of commercial and cultural relations between the Soviet Union and Poland has achieved new and more favorable conditions than before. We have always attached great political significance to this. Practical cooperation between the Soviet Union and France has progressed smoothly. The visit of French dignitaries to the Soviet Union and the establishment of closer and more commercial contacts between the two countries have made it easier to develop this cooperation. We believe that Soviet-French cooperation has entered a new stage and will have good results in the future. Finally, we have concluded a treaty of non-aggression, neutrality, and friendship with Italy. At the same time, at the initiative of Spain and Uruguay, we have established diplomatic relations with them. These are also clear examples of the Soviet Union's development of diplomatic relations with other countries."

Relations with Britain Improve After Deteriorating Once

"On the contrary, our relations with Britain deteriorated briefly this year. For obvious reasons, the Soviet government could not agree to a policy of using external force to suppress our internal affairs. At the same time, it was able to maintain its position throughout this incident. This deterioration was caused by the trial of the Vickers company saboteurs. It was soon eliminated. Normal commercial negotiations are now underway in London."

Safeguarding Peace, the Policy Remains Unchanged

"Soviet-German relations have always occupied a special position in our country's international relations. The Soviet Union's commitment to the principles of safeguarding world peace and our country's independence has no reason to change its policy towards Germany. However, the rulers of Germany have repeatedly tried to change their relationship with the Soviet Union this year. Clear-headed people can easily see this tendency. At this time, we do not need to describe in detail the statements made by Luxembourg, Hugenberg, and other people. They have been fully described in writing and orally in this country. One thing that we can clearly see is that until recently, the friendship between the Soviet Union and Germany was based on the mutual desire for peace and the development of economic relations. Even today, we absolutely remain committed to these principles. We believe that only by pursuing these principles can we create the power of political and economic cooperation between the Soviet Union and Germany and the power to seek world peace. However, the leaders of the militaristic national socialist ideology, such as Luxembourg, are the opposite. Their policies are entirely permeated by reactionary desires and imperialist plundering plans. Therefore, they are incompatible with every consolidation and friendship of the Soviet Union. We also believe that this policy is incompatible with Germany's great future."

It is Not Enough to Speak of Goodwill with Japan, Whose Cunning Cannot Be Hidden

"As for our relations with Japan, they have been discussed in great detail. The Soviet government's policy on this point is clear to those outside the Soviet Union. We initially requested the conclusion of a non-aggression pact, agreed to sell the Middle East Railway, and dealt with various commercial issues, such as the issue of Japan's privileges in the Far East, with a sincere attitude. These facts are well known to everyone. At the same time, no one can ask us to provide greater evidence of our peaceful intentions. However, all this has not prevented some Japanese newspapers and Japanese officials from fabricating various dirty rumors every day, claiming that the Soviet Union has aggressive intentions. One day they issued a message saying that the Soviet Union's political police attacked the Manchurian border. The next day they said that Moscow sent people to China to organize anti-Japanese movements, etc. They issue more rumors every day. The purpose of this action is nothing more than to cover up the anti-Soviet Union and anti-Soviet provocations of their agents. The most reactionary military personnel in Japan are particularly afraid of the establishment of considerable cooperation between the Soviet Union, the United States, and China to deal with the elements that initiate hostilities in the Far East, given their own increasing isolation. They exaggerate the possibility of this kind of cooperation, and at the same time, they expose themselves by denying the rumors they have fabricated in a panic. They are extremely afraid of the Soviet Union's huge growth. At the same time, they lose their confidence and declare with an even more stubborn attitude "This is the time!" All the above is sufficient to show that they cannot be indifferent to the danger of equality for war and aggression. Is there a need to state this matter for our meaning now? What we need to state here has already been said. Our task is to continue to implement the peace policy in the Far East unyieldingly and improve our relations with Japan. At the same time, we must be fully prepared to cope with possible attacks and disturbances. As far as the current situation is concerned, we are sincerely and unfortunately still unable to guarantee that we can avoid these attacks and disturbances."

Germany and Japan Have Different Intentions in Withdrawing from the League of Nations

"The so-called danger of a new war is particularly certain this year, as evidenced by the following facts: Germany and Japan have both approved their withdrawal from the League of Nations. Germany's move is clearly related to its desire to expand its armaments. It considers participation in the League of Nations as one of the obstacles to expanding its armaments. When Japan informed the international community of its withdrawal, it stated that it wanted to maintain its complete freedom to intervene in China. Even the League of Nations, to some extent, allows the interventionists the freedom to act. However, it must also be recognized that the fact that the League of Nations has a certain hindering effect on the forces of military expansion is a favorable fact. No matter how different the reasons for withdrawing from the League of Nations are, what we need to consider is the following fact, namely, that these important events cannot help consolidate world peace. On the contrary, they can allow the most reactionary and aggressive forces to run wild. Therefore, we must safeguard peace more resolutely and systematically. At the same time, we must use the various opportunities that exist to expose all attempts to promote new imperialist wars and new aggressive actions against the Soviet Union."

Gathering the Power of Workers and Peasants to Awaken the Imperial Dreams

"Our most important task is to inform the working masses of the Soviet Union's true position in the current capitalist environment. Therefore, the basic facts that threaten peace, as well as the facts that can promote our peace policy and world peace, should be accurately informed to the broad masses of workers and peasants. The ruling classes of capitalist countries have never been able and will never be able to inform their people of the actual situation of their respective countries and the actual foreign policies of their respective governments. This is even more difficult for the gentlemen in the reactionary fascist camp. They are still entangled in the dreams of imperialist plunder. Therefore, they will ultimately insist on the attitude that their heads can be cut off but this policy cannot be changed. Only the Soviet government, which is most supported by the workers and peasants, firmly believes that developing the conscious attitude of the masses towards peace is its greatest task and obligation. This is where our greatest strength lies at this time. When the workers and peasants understand what the purpose of their struggle is, what they are working for, striving for, and sacrificing for, then they will never be afraid of difficulties and will become an irresistible force (enthusiastic applause). It is with unwavering faith that we Bolsheviks move forward bravely (enthusiastic applause)." (29th Tass Dispatch)

Stalin Discusses the Crisis in Japanese-Russian Relations

Friendship Cannot Be Achieved Alone

Japan Will Only Bring Trouble Upon Itself if It Does Not Change Its Attitude

(New York) Today's New York Times published a conversation between Soviet Russia's Stalin and its Moscow correspondent, saying that Stalin has clearly declared that Japan is a real danger to the Soviet Union. Stalin's words said, "I think it would be most unwise for Japan to attempt to attack the Soviet Union at this time. However, our country must be prepared for the worst. We want to have friendly relations with the Japanese. Unfortunately, this is not something that our country can achieve unilaterally. If more rational elements can gain power in Japan and make more cautious suggestions, then the two countries will be able to coexist peacefully. I am afraid that Japan's warlords will force the more sober policies to retreat. Therefore, there is a serious danger at the moment. We cannot but prepare to deal with it." In addition, Stalin also said that the Soviet Union will support the League of Nations in maintaining world peace and wants to increase trade relations with other countries. As for the resumption of diplomatic relations between the United States and Russia, Stalin said that they are a sales market and are also prepared to order a large amount of foreign goods and pay for them. The Soviet Union's repayment of debts at this time is surprising to everyone. But the Soviet Union is able to repay its debts. He knows that non-repayment of debts is everywhere today, but other countries may default on their debts, while the Soviet Union will not default. The Soviet Union has a very rich gold reserve, and the amount of mining is increasing day by day. It has now mined more than 100 million rubles, more than double the gold production of the Imperial Russian era." According to reports, Stalin rarely speaks and rarely meets with foreign journalists. Therefore, this conversation is extremely noticed by Americans. (29th Kuomintang Dispatch)

France Threatens to Expose German Military Secrets

Poncet to Return to Berlin with Reply

Seeking Compromise Based on Anglo-French Agreement

Disarmament Negotiations Must Take Place in Geneva

(Paris) According to news from here today, the French government plans to publish a secret document at the League of Nations meeting, which is likely to cause great international shock. It is now believed that this document concerns Germany's military strength and other miscellaneous matters. French Ambassador to Germany Poncet arrived here today from Berlin and plans to carry back to Germany the French government's reply to Hitler's proposal for direct negotiations on disarmament and the Saar issue. It is heard that France's policy aims to reach a compromise in Geneva based on the plan agreed upon by French Foreign Minister Pong and British Foreign Minister Simon in September of this year. If Germany rejects this plan, France intends to reveal Germany's secrets before the League of Nations Council meeting. The French reply rejects direct Franco-German meetings and declares that France advocates disarmament but not rearmament, and advocates discussions in Geneva but not elsewhere. (Reuters, 28th)

(Paris) French Ambassador to Germany Poncet returned here this morning. At 3 p.m., he met with Foreign Minister Pong. The Foreign Minister gave Poncet the instructions passed by yesterday's cabinet meeting. These instructions are in response to Germany's request for rearmament. In addition to the instructions, there are also other useful explanations attached. Poncet plans to rush back to Berlin to attend the diplomatic reception on New Year's Day. As for the French government's memorandum to German Chancellor Hitler, it is planned to be delivered after the New Year holidays on January 4th or 5th. Foreign Minister Pong also met with the Soviet and Polish ambassadors to France today. The purpose of the meeting was probably to inform the two ambassadors of the cabinet meeting's decisions regarding Franco-German relations and the outline of the memorandum to Hitler. In addition to the two ambassadors, Pong also met with U.S. Ambassador to Russia Bullitt. (Havas, 28th)

(Paris) The French cabinet has already drafted a memorandum on Germany's demand for rearmament and handed it over to Ambassador Poncet for delivery to the German government. The content of this memorandum is still unknown. It is generally believed that the French government considers Germany's various demands to be completely contrary to the disarmament conference. The French government believes that international security can only be built within the scope of the League of Nations and through the means of reducing armaments. The French government also intends to resubmit the proposals decided upon during the talks with Britain on September 23rd and 24th, namely that once a general disarmament convention is signed, the French government will propose to reduce the number of bomber aircraft by half, but only on the condition that other related countries also make the same promise. (Havas, 28th)

Meeting Between Mussolini and Simon Scheduled

For January 4th

(London) The talks between Italian Prime Minister Mussolini and British Foreign Secretary Simon have now been scheduled for January 4th of the following year. Mr. Drummond has arrived in Capri today to meet with Mr. Simon. (National News Agency, 28th)

Britain and France United Against Germany

Brussels: A dispatch from the "Belgian News Agency" correspondent in Paris states that Belgian Foreign Minister Hymans met with Lord Tyrell, the British Ambassador to France, today. Tyrell explained to the Belgian Foreign Minister the outline of the British reply to Germany's proposals. The so-called German proposals are those recently put forward by German Foreign Minister Neurath during his meeting with the British Ambassador to Germany. The gist of the British reply is that Britain believes that negotiations on disarmament should continue within the scope of the League of Nations. The amount of German troops should also be calculated according to the numbers listed in the League of Nations Yearbook, and the numbers listed in the plan submitted by Britain to the Disarmament Conference should be used as the basis. (Havas, 28th)

Hymans Makes Statement After Meeting with French Authorities

(Paris) After meeting with French authorities, Belgian Foreign Minister Hymans made a statement to the press, saying that the talks were very frank and cordial, avoiding all formalities. Foreign Minister Pong and Premier Xu had specially studied the disarmament issue with him. Hymans particularly stated on this point that Belgium's greatest concern is to find ways to avoid competition in disarmament, because competition in armaments will make it difficult to restore international credit and economic activity, and the end result will inevitably lead to a major war, the situation of which will be far more terrifying than the European War of 1914. The danger is that the hearts of Britain and Italy to avoid it, it is presumed that it is no less than France and Belgium. Belgium, as one of the countries most threatened by war, regards the disarmament issue as a matter of national survival, so it sincerely hopes that the negotiations conducted by the countries can reach a basis for compromise, so that the disarmament conference can continue to be beneficial work and can establish an international compromise to prevent the competition of armaments and increase the guarantee of peace.

Hymans also said that small countries like Belgium are all attached to the League of Nations, thinking that even if the League of Nations can not but have changes, then the various principles contained in the covenant should be maintained, and especially the equality of countries in law. Finally, talking about economic issues, Hymans said that he hopes that France's new policy of import quantity restrictions can increase trade between the two countries. Hymans also said that since the economic organizations of France and Belgium are both the same, and have strictly adhered to the gold standard policy, the two countries should be combined on monetary issues, to show each other's solidarity in the economy. (Havas, 28th)

US Treasury Orders Civilians to Turn In Hidden Gold

Soliciting Gold to Concentrate in the National Treasury

Prelude to Implementing the Thomas Plan

(Washington) The acting Secretary of the Treasury, Morgenthau, today ordered that all gold coins, gold bullion, and gold certificates held by the public, with a few exceptions, be immediately turned over to the government in full, in exchange for other currencies at the legal official price of $20.67 per ounce. The regulations are exempted only for (1) gold licensed by the Treasury, (2) antique coins collected by collectors, but gold coins worth $2.50 each are still not covered by this rule, (3) small gold nuggets and gold filings that have not been melted and whose value does not exceed $100, and gold used for industrial or decorative purposes or gold needed for professional use (4) gold coins, gold bullion, and gold certificates held by the Federal Reserve Bank and the Financial Relief Corporation, (5) gold and foreign currency held by residents of the Philippines, Guam, Samoa, Hawaii, the Panama Canal Zone, Puerto Rico, and the Virgin Islands, but only if they do not reside in the continental United States or engage in industry and commerce in the continental United States. As for the method of submitting to the government, those who hold gold coins, gold bullion, or gold certificates can send them to the Federal Reserve Bank and its branches or member banks for collection, and at the same time send a letter to the Treasury Department informing them of the return situation. After the Treasury Department obtains a report from the collecting agency to prove it, it will exchange it for other currencies at the statutory gold price. If it is gold bars or gold bullion, although the Financial Relief Corporation is currently buying newly mined gold at a price of $34.06 per ounce, the Treasury Department will still convert it into common currency at the official price of $20.67. According to the previous presidential order prohibiting the hoarding of gold, people were still allowed to hoard gold or gold certificates worth less than $100, but now this gold is also turned over to the government. It is heard that the gold coins and gold certificates currently remaining in the hands of the public still amount to $528,531,814. In the future, except for those abroad, most of them will be turned over to the government. After the previous presidential order prohibiting the hoarding of gold, the court ruled that the president's order exceeded his authority based on the National Congress's authorization to the Treasury Department to recover gold. Therefore, this time the order was issued by the Treasury Department. As for the intention of this move, the Treasury Department did not explain it. It is expected that it will be to strictly enforce the prohibition of gold hoarding, or it may be a prelude to confiscating all the gold in the country, including that held by the Federal Reserve Bureau, and implementing the Thomas plan to reset the value of gold. A few days ago, the President ordered the Acting Secretary of the Treasury and the Attorney General to jointly study the Thomas plan. This plan stipulates that the government confiscates all the gold in the country, gives it the statutory official price, and then sets the value of gold at 41 yuan and 34 minutes, twice the appropriate official price. It is estimated that the government can make a profit of 300 million yuan in one transfer, and the price of gold yuan will also be halved. According to Mr. Thomas, he will submit it to the National Congress. (National News Agency, 28th)

Scottish Loch Ness Monster Appears From Time to Time

Some Say It's an Ancient Mosasaur

Arousing Research by Naturalists

(London) The Loch Ness Monster has become famous in various countries. Professor Gruvaner of the Paris Museum of Natural History said that this beast is of the Megophias class. The French gunboat a number once encountered this type of strange beast three times outside Vietnam in 1898, with a body length of 75 feet. However, German Professor Borsig believes that this animal is likely an ancient mosasaur, belonging to the marine lizard class. People today believe that their species has become extinct. Several regions in Italy are now claiming that they also have this thing in their territory. Recently, one was shot in Sicily, and after investigation, it turned out to be a large, non-toxic snake. It is now learned that the strange object in Loch Ness has recently appeared from time to time, but the size of its body is described differently by those who see it. (Reuters, 29th)

French Merchants Suspect Transshipment Tax System

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance received information that timber transported from abroad in the three northeastern provinces has been subject to a 5.5% transshipment tax. Since the promulgation of the method of collecting taxes in different places after the Northeast Customs was seized, it has been stipulated that timber, because it is impossible to identify its source, should be included in the category of import duties. Recently, the French Minister, Wiliton, wrote to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs stating that the wood veneer factory of French merchants transported wood from the three northeastern provinces, passed through Tianjin, and was transferred to Shanghai by workers. The various taxes paid reached 26 and a half percent of the original price of the goods, which was unbearable. He requested consultation with the Ministry of Finance for relief. The Ministry of Finance believed that the sections described in the French merchants' request seemed to be not well aware of the tax collection methods and the current transshipment tax system after the closure of the customs of the eastern provinces, and it was not convenient to grant reductions and exemptions for the taxes to be collected, which would be inconsistent with the general customs regulations. Public Bus Tickets Temporarily Postponed for Stamp Duty

Customs Patrol Vessels Change Signals for Inspecting Ships

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance received information that the regulations for customs patrol vessels inspecting Chinese and foreign ships stipulate that when customs patrol vessels order civilian vessels or civilian ships to stop at sea for inspection, they emit three short whistle blasts and one long whistle blast, day or night. This is the same as the international maritime signal code for seeking assistance from other ships or asking them not to move away, which is easy to cause misunderstandings. In order to comply with international practice, the signal issued by customs patrol vessels ordering ships to stop has been changed to first sounding one short whistle blast, one long whistle blast, and then two short whistle blasts. Yesterday, the Inspector General of Customs was ordered to instruct all customs offices to comply, and at the same time, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs was requested to notify the governments of various countries to take note. (Special Dispatch, 29th)

China National Aviation Corporation Strives to Complete Three Major Air Routes

(Nanjing) Dai Siji, the manager of China National Aviation Corporation, stated that the company's contract with the United States has reached three years, and past performance is still commendable. This year, the company is dedicated to completing three major air routes. The Shanghai-Beiping route was opened on January 10th of this year, the Chongqing-Chengdu route was opened on November 11th of this year, and the Shanghai-Guangdong route was opened on October 24th of this year. From then on, the north-south and east-west routes are connected, providing convenience for Chinese and foreign people. The Chongqing-Chengdu route is especially convenient. Previously, it took ten days to travel between Chengdu and Chongqing by both land and water. After the air route opened, it only takes two hours to travel over a thousand li. The people of the country feel that the Shu Road is no longer difficult. The company plans to use the latest type of aircraft for flights between Shanghai, Hankou, Chongqing, and Chengdu next summer, as business is booming and passenger and postal services are developing. This type of aircraft is stable and comfortable, with a cruising speed of 150 miles per hour (approximately 450 li), which is one-third faster than the current aircraft. It can arrive from Shanghai to Hankou in the morning and deliver all the mail in the afternoon, and then leave Hankou the next morning and arrive in Chengdu at noon. The journey between Shanghai and Chengdu is only two days, and only ten hours in the air. From January to the end of November of the twenty-second year, the company carried a total of 2,349 passengers, totaling 819,693 miles, and carried 40,767 kilograms of mail. (29th Dispatch)
