Kong Bandit Peeps at Nanchang and is Defeated

Fierce Battle at Wanshou Palace in Xishan Lasts a Day and Night

Each Army Encircles and Suppresses the Bandit, Preventing Him from Returning to His Old Nest

Nanchang Correspondence: Kong Hechong's fake Sixth Army Corps was fiercely attacked by He Jian's troops in Ganzhou West Wanzai and had nowhere to go. Therefore, a part of the force fled to Hunan South, and a part secretly entered Qingjiang on the 24th. The Kong bandits looted in the county for only a few hours, and the chasing army had already arrived, so the bandits immediately withdrew and fled north to Xinjian. At noon on the 26th, 4,000 to 5,000 bandits were also discovered on the Xishan Wanshou Palace side, with about 2,000 to 3,000 guns. The authorities ordered the Wei Regiment to suppress them. The vanguard encountered the bandits on the Xishan foothills north of Wanshou Palace. Both sides exchanged fire, with bullets raining down. Airplanes soared over Xishan, dropping bombs to assist in the battle, killing many bandits. However, the Wei Regiment retreated slightly due to the disparity in numbers. That night, the bandits fled to the west of Shengmi, 30 li from Niuhang Station. The General Headquarters immediately dispatched troops to cross the river and reinforce the west from Niuhang in the dim light of night. At the same time, the garrison troops in Gaoan also went east to pursue and suppress, taking a three-sided converging formation. On the 27th, as dawn approached, the bloody battle continued until 3:00 or 4:00 PM. Because the bandits had too many casualties, they retreated from Wanshou Palace in the northwest of Xinjian one after another. The air force flew to pursue and bomb them, killing even more bandits. By evening, the bandits fled in a panic from the Gaoan border towards the northwest. In addition to ordering each unit to pursue closely, the General Headquarters also mobilized certain units from the western route to block the bandits in separate directions, ensuring that they could not retreat to their old nests on the border of Jiangxi, Hubei, and Hunan, and planned to encircle and annihilate the bandits in a certain location. Recently, a telegram was received from Niuhang reporting the victory, stating that the Kong bandits had already fled far away, and that more than 600 bandits were killed in the battle. (Evening of December 27)

Remnant Bandits in Ezhou South Return and Flee to the Border of Hunan and Jiangxi

Chongyang County City is Saved from Danger

Bandits Fleeing to Ezhou East Have Been Surrounded

Hankou Correspondence: Kong Hechong's bandit forces, the fake 16th and 17th Armies, have recently fled from the border of Hunan and Jiangxi to Ezhou South in succession. Chongyang County City is in imminent danger, and the traffic on the Hunan-Ezhou Road is often cut off. After Chen Jicheng arrived in Puqi, representatives from various places petitioned one after another. Chen publicly stated that he had ordered Guo Rudong and Xiao Zhichu to each allocate elite troops to assist Feng Xingxian's division in suppressing the bandits, and that he had a thorough plan to eliminate the bandits, guaranteeing that the security of each county would be worry-free. Sure enough, within a few days, the bandits were defeated, Chongyang was saved from danger, and the bandits, unable to invade, looted in Hongxia, Zhulin Ao, Zhongxing Gai, and Jinshi Guan, and continued to flee back to the border of Hunan and Jiangxi. Chen then dispatched Feng Xingxian's and Li Dingwu's two units as pursuit forces, tracking and pursuing the bandits. At the same time, he telegraphed the garrison troops on the border of Hunan and Jiangxi to effectively block them, implementing a joint suppression by the three provinces. Chen, believing that the defenses of Puqi and Chongyang were solid, returned to Hankou on the armored train on the evening of the 27th. On the 28th, he visited Cao Haosen, the chief of staff of the General Headquarters, and He Chengyu, the appeasement director, to report on the progress, and returned to Daye that evening to prevent fires. The remnant bandits in the border area of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, led by bandit leader Wu Huanxian, fled to Henan South and Anhui West, and have now returned to Ezhou East. One group is in Laojun Mountain and Tiantai Mountain in Huang'an, and the other is in Guangyu Mountain in Macheng. Xiao Zhichu, the commander of the 26th Army, sent troops to encircle and suppress the bandits in four directions. On the 27th, Xiao telegraphed the victory to Hankou, saying, "According to reliable reports, Wu Huanxian, the commander of the fake 25th Army, gathered about 2,000 remnants and fled from Henan to the Tiantai Mountain and Laojun Mountain area northwest of Huang'an around the Yangjing days of this month. I immediately ordered Wang's Brigade Commander Zhang Chi, stationed in Hekou Town, to lead two battalions of troops to suppress the bandits from Huajiahe. Chen's Brigade Commander Chuan, stationed in Qiliping, sent a battalion of troops to attack the bandits from the side. Li's Brigade Commander Yinchen, stationed in Huangpi Station, led two battalions of troops to assist in the suppression. Hao's Regiment, stationed in Xuanhuadian, sent a battalion of troops to guerilla towards the southeast to prevent the bandits from fleeing. Each suppression unit launched a simultaneous attack on the You Day. On that day, Li Yinchen's regiment encountered 500 to 600 remnants of the fake 73rd Division of the bandits in Tiantai Hougou, more than ten li north of Tiantai Mountain. They were given a severe attack. The bandits initially relied on the mountains to resist stubbornly, but after our army divided its troops to raid them, many were killed, and the remaining bandits fled to the northeast Dazhuyuan area. On the same day, our Hao Regiment's Liu Battalion patrolled from Xuanhuadian to the Heidouzai in the southeast. According to reports, the fake Ezhou Northeast Road Committee is now in Dazhuyuan, and the fake 25th Army and the fake 75th Division are in the southeast area of Hujiahe, with a total of about 1,000 people. Currently, each suppression unit is continuing to search and suppress the bandits. I heard that Xiao Zhichu was grateful." (December 28)

He Jian Telegraphed an Order to Execute Yu Yizhong

Yu Claimed to be the Commander-in-Chief of the All-People's Army

Fang Dingying Was Used by the Min Party to Disturb Hunan

Changsha Correspondence: At the beginning of the Fujian Incident, Yu Yizhong, the leader of the Hunan branch of the Social Democratic Party, was instigated by the Fujian side, carrying 100,000 yuan to Hunan West to mobilize He Jingcheng, the commander of the First Regiment of the Fourth Security District, and the greenwoodsmen in Hunan West, occupying the counties of Qianyang and Huitong, and carrying out a rebellion. He claimed to be the All-People's National Salvation Army, with Yu Yizhong as the commander-in-chief, He Jingcheng as the commander of the First Division, Long Hongjun as the commander of the Second Division, and Lu Xin as the commander of the Third Division. At the beginning of the previous month, he led thousands of troops to attack Hongjiang. After the Brigade Commander Chen Zixian and Deputy Brigade Commander Xie Long supervised three regiments of soldiers to meet the attack, a fierce battle lasted for two days, and they were defeated. The counties of Qianyang and Huitong were also recovered. Yu, He, and others led the remnants and fled to the border of Qianzhou. At that time, Long Hongjun and Yang Zhennan (who was He Jingcheng's regiment commander) voluntarily surrendered and defected from the rebel army. Chen Zixian reported this to He Jian for approval and reorganization, and appointed Long and Yang as regiment commanders, stationed in their original defenses to await orders. After Yu, He, and others fled to the border of Qianzhou, they colluded with Qiu Yihua and other greenwoodsmen in various places on the border of Hunan and Qianzhou, hoping to rise again. Fang Dingying, who had previously served as the army commander of the Revolutionary Army, came from Fujian with a large amount of money to encourage Yu, He, and others to attack Hongjiang again. On the 12th of this month, they launched an attack from Huang County towards Qianyang and Huitong. On the evening of the 24th, they made contact with He Peilin's regiment of Chen Brigade in Anjiang, forty or fifty li from Hongjiang. He's regiment was surrounded because they were unfamiliar with the terrain. On the morning of the 25th, He's regiment desperately charged, and after a fierce battle until noon, they turned defeat into victory, broke the encirclement, and defeated more than 2,000 troops of Yu, He, and others. Yu Yizhong, the commander-in-chief of the All-People's National Salvation Army, was captured alive, and Fang Dingying, He Jingcheng, and others led the remnants and fled to the border of Qianzhou and Huangzhou. Yu Yizhong was sent to Hongjiang by He's regiment on the 26th. He Jian, upon receiving the report, immediately telegraphed an order to execute him on the spot and send his head to the province for public display. He also telegraphed Deputy Brigade Commander Xie Long to lead two regiments of soldiers to suppress the bandits via Jiangkou and Gulouping, and ordered He's regiment to follow up from Anjiang Daping to Qianzhou and Huangzhou, hoping to annihilate them in one fell swoop. The following is the victory telegram from Chen Brigade: "Our He Peilin regiment camped in Anjiang last night. The fake commander-in-chief Yu Yizhong gathered the remnants of He (Jingcheng) and Qiu (Yihua), about 2,000 people and guns, and launched a full-scale attack. Our He regiment was surrounded because they were unfamiliar with the terrain. The battle was extremely fierce from the next morning until noon. Finally, our He regiment desperately charged and completely defeated the bandits. The fake commander-in-chief Yu Yizhong was captured on the spot by the Fifth Company of He's regiment, and more than 100 bandits and more than 100 guns were captured. We also suffered dozens of casualties of officers and soldiers. In addition to ordering the regiment to send Yu to Hongjiang and proceed according to plan, I hereby telegraph the report. Details will be reported later. Yours sincerely, Chen Zixian." He Jian replied: "To Brigade Commander Chen of Hongjiang, He's regiment has made great efforts in combat and is worthy of commendation. After Yu is sent to Hongjiang, he will be executed on the spot, and his head will be sent to the province to please the people. A list of all the officers and soldiers who contributed will be reported for awards and compensation. We still rely on you to supervise and encourage the various units to work hard to suppress and eliminate the root causes. He Jian." (December 27)

The Incident at the Tianjin Naval Hospital is Resolved

Liu Ruiheng Negotiates in Peiping and Tianjin

Reaches a New Agreement with the French Side

Regarding the incident at the Beiyang Naval Medical School Hospital, the Executive Yuan recently sent Liu Ruiheng to Peiping and Tianjin to meet with representatives from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Navy, and the French ambassador and French consul to negotiate a settlement. As a result, the agreement previously signed by Zhang Xueliang was cancelled, and a new agreement was reached. Liu Ruiheng released the following statement regarding this case:

"The Tianjin Beiyang Naval Medical School Hospital was founded in the Qing Dynasty and has been in existence for 53 years. The address was within the official land at that time. After the Boxer Rebellion, France opened a concession according to the treaty. The school hospital happened to be within the concession. Because it was official land, the French side believed that it belonged to the concession. After negotiations, conditions were proposed, such as hiring French teachers, and there was a saying that a silver tael of rent must be paid every year. It was then continued to be operated. Since the Republic of China, it has been transferred to the jurisdiction of the Ministry of the Navy. In the past six or seven years, due to lack of funds, a lot of salary was owed to Chinese and French teachers. The medical school was closed long ago, and the hospital was also badly damaged. This spring, Zhang Xueliang of the Peiping Military Branch negotiated with the French side to sell the land base in order to raise military expenses. The French side intended to deduct the cost of opening roads and various outstanding funds and donations after the price was changed, so there was not much left. However, this contract was signed by Zhang's representative and the French Consul on February 15, 22nd year. When this news came out, all parties believed that the real estate should not be disposed of by the Military Branch, and after so many years of the school and hospital, the cancellation caused widespread opposition. In April, the Executive Yuan decided to restore the school and hospital. The government will prepare funds to acknowledge the debt, rebuild it, and continue to operate it. Therefore, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of the Navy dispatched representatives to Tianjin to negotiate with the French Consul to cancel the contract. The French Consul delayed and prevaricated about the cancellation of the agreement for many days. On the 9th of this month, the Executive Yuan ordered me to go to Peiping and Tianjin to meet with representatives from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Navy to resolve this matter. After I arrived in Tianjin, I met with the French Ambassador Weilitun and the French Consul Libisi. After a week of negotiations, the new agreement was drafted on the 17th. I immediately telegraphed the report to the Executive Yuan. The agreement was signed at 7:00 PM that evening. The main points of the new agreement are that 24 acres of land are designated for the Beiyang Naval Medical School Hospital for restoration, and 15 acres are used for opening new roads and providing road maintenance expenses. The Chinese government is responsible for repaying the arrears of French teachers' salaries, while the arrears of Chinese teachers' salaries will be handled separately by the Chinese and French parties through the exchange of letters. The full text of the contract has been approved by this session of the Executive Yuan meeting, and it has been resolved to set up a preparatory committee for the revival of the hospital and school, which will be organized by the four ministries of Interior, Finance, Education, and Navy to plan and handle the matter. The arrears of French teachers' salaries will be paid from the French Gengzi indemnity, and the arrears of Chinese teachers' salaries will be handled by the Ministry of Education and the Ministry of Finance. This matter can now be concluded for the time being. Regarding the negotiation process, there are still some things that need to be added. First, the general outline of the contract was determined by the Executive Yuan meeting in advance. Second, the conditions originally proposed by the French side, such as repaying the arrears of French teachers' salaries with the land price and donating funds to the Pasteur Laboratory, have been removed. Third, in fact, there is no possibility of a better outcome. The dispute has reached this point and has been exhausted. I have paid great attention to the arrears of Chinese teachers' salaries and have submitted them to the Executive Yuan meeting for exchange of letters. The Yuan has now transferred the matter to the Ministry of Education and the Ministry of Finance, which will naturally be settled and can be expected to be repaid. The revival of the medical school and hospital is very important and should be organized and handled by the preparatory committee as soon as possible. I sincerely hope to see it completed soon."

Inspection Tour of Jiangxi, Anhui, Hunan, and Hubei (Special Correspondent Ren An)

The Old Social System Once Destroyed

Lease Terms Becoming More Lenient

Huo Shan Correspondence: The Huo Shan Red Disaster, for more than four years, with repeated proposals to abolish land boundaries, ultimately failed to materialize. When they divided the land, destroyed the houses of landlords and gentry, opposed ancestral halls, eradicated superstition, and overthrew various old social systems, the peasants initially felt unaccustomed and wanted to flee. However, due to the tight organization and strict precautions taken by the Red bandits and various levels of puppet Soviet governments, they were unable to fulfill their wishes. Over time, they gradually became accustomed to it. The unscrupulous ones even acted as accomplices, causing various inconveniences to the National Army's suppression efforts. The remaining bandits in western Anhui were not easily eradicated, and this was the reason. Their land distribution system was based on productivity as the standard. Red bandits, Red bandit family members, and political workers of the puppet Soviet government first chose the fertile land and devoured it, and then gradually extended to others. After obtaining land, they had to fulfill obligations such as being requisitioned and performing various tasks. The amount of requisitioned items was always increased or decreased based on the abundance of the harvest. Ordinary people paid about one liter of grain per month to supply the Red bandits. Landlords and punished rich peasants, even if they became beggars, had to hand over any items they obtained each day that exceeded their daily living needs, without waiting to be requisitioned. Otherwise, they would be charged with concealing wealth and harboring evil without repentance. Ordinary poor farmers and workers were considered the best elements, and their words and deeds were relatively free. Even if they made mistakes, they were often forgiven. However, if rich peasants or intellectuals violated the law, they were severely punished without leniency.

The puppet Soviet government was organized with the village as the unit, with a chairman, also called the village head. Above the village was the township, with five or seven committee members in charge of land, labor, economy, culture, and food. The district and county organizations were the same as the township. However, in addition to various committees, the county also had a Political Security Bureau. The bureau had a revolutionary court that specialized in hearing cases against those who opposed the Red bandits. The bureau was located in Zhufo Town, seventy or eighty miles from the city, and was directly under the Northwest District Committee of the puppet government, wielding great power. The members who joined the Red Party before 1919, who initially led the riots in various villages, were all suspected of corruption by last year and were sentenced to death on charges of being members of the Reorganization Faction, AB Corps, or Reactionary Faction, numbering several thousands. The biggest reason for the failure of the Communist bandits was this self-inflicted slaughter. The mass grave of ten thousand people in that town is where the bodies of those killed in this massacre were buried, stained with blood and piled with white bones, a truly tragic sight. The outbreak of the Red Disaster in that area was initially due to the general influence of the Northern Expedition on young people, who all strived to engage in party affairs and conducted widespread propaganda in the countryside. Their central slogans were only "25% rent reduction," the abolition of "　Chicken," "Sauce Wheat," and "New Rice" (these were all customary gifts that local tenants had to send to landlords in addition to paying rent, namely sending chickens on New Year's Eve called "　Chicken," sending wheat when landlords made sauce in summer or winter called "Sauce Wheat," and selecting drooping ears of newly ripened grain, baking them dry, and grinding them into rice to send to the landlord to taste the new crop called "New Rice," the amount depending on the generosity or stinginess of the landlord), and "landlords must transport rental grain themselves," etc. Farmers usually paid too much rent and had to deliver it from far and wide, accumulating resentment that they dared not speak out. Hearing these slogans, they could not help but be moved and gradually protested to the landlords. The landlords and gentry deeply resented these propagandizing youths and drove them into hiding in the countryside, which was exploited by the Red bandits to conduct secret work, eventually leading to a major disaster, killing those who disagreed with them. It is said that the vast majority of those killed were the very people who first advocated the riots.

In addition to the National Army's four encirclement and suppression campaigns and the Red bandits' self-slaughter, they also stepped up the organization of children's groups, Red Guards, women's comfort teams, etc., turning farming families that should have been enjoying family happiness into nests of partings. In particular, encouraging young men to become bandits easily aroused dissatisfaction in the boudoirs. There was a so-called "Shepherd's Song," with lyrics like "My husband's revolution is true, the revolution has been two or three springs, scattering a family, husband in the south, wife in the north, the two of us separated by tears." Although the sentences are simple, they are very popular, which also shows a glimpse of the separation of flesh and blood and private resentment among the people in the bandit areas at that time. However, the Communist bandits, constrained by the situation, did not show weakness and also sang a song, "My wife doesn't have to worry, although it is difficult now, we must talk about the group, since I have come, you should also do it, love will not be hurt." There are two other songs, one is "The White Army is the real bandit, following the local tyrants to kill and destroy indiscriminately, a mess, showing off their power and prestige, we workers and peasants all suffer," which is used to slander the National Army and to warn workers and peasants to be conscious and make their own decisions. The other is "Widow is young, wants to marry, mother-in-law and both families, have not explained, there is a person behind the mountain, he is young, and I like him, no money to marry, come to the side of the road, two eyes full of tears, look up and see the Communist Party members, Party members say good, equal women, find themselves, find a good man, who can farm, and ride horses and sit in sedan chairs." This is to persuade young widows to choose their own husbands and marry. In addition, there are many tea-picking tunes and children's songs, but they are not as popular or as deeply impressive as the above three songs. Even farmers and women who have been married for more than a year can still recite them with a smile, but they dare not recite the important sentences.

According to the county magistrate, the current social situation is becoming more stable. There is only one civil lawsuit every ten days or so, mostly related to "touching melons" (a euphemism for theft). In the northwest township, which is adjacent to Lihuang County, several assassination cases have recently occurred, all of which are local gentry, such as heads of baojia (a system of local administration). They were suddenly intercepted and killed, and there was no way to solve the cases. Rich merchants, in particular, are trembling with fear, secretly carrying opium paste to prevent being kidnapped and to commit suicide if misfortune befalls them. This is because, on the one hand, the township is wary of the remaining bandits in Lihuang County who may come to harass them from time to time, and on the other hand, the surrendered and reformed people are arrogant and unruly, and may occasionally relapse into old habits, or because landlords may retaliate for past grievances, which can easily lead to assassinations. In the southeast township, there are real bandits who rob merchants, big and small, and sometimes even fight with small groups of Red bandits, presumably to seize weapons from each other.

Huo Shan's education has never been developed. The number of literate people is far less than that of Liu'an. During the Red period, hundreds of Lenin elementary schools were established. At the beginning of the recovery, the army converted them into short-term compulsory elementary schools and reformatories, extensively recruiting surrendered and reformed elements and providing them with special education, with remarkable results. It was hoped that they would be converted into formal elementary schools to educate tens of thousands of school-age children. Unexpectedly, each school and institute only operated for one term and then stopped abruptly. Currently, there are only two or three public and private elementary schools in the city, and all the four townships are missing. The county government has repeatedly ordered the preparation, but it is still indifferent due to lack of funding. However, the customs are simple, and the opium scourge is also light. The social economy is not difficult to recover. The county government officials are neatly dressed, adhere to office hours, and have a strong sense of service, which is commendable.

Several years ago, the value of land rose to 300 yuan per picul, and even the lower grades were around 200 yuan. When leasing land, the "deposit money" (i.e., rent deposit) paid by tenants to landlords was as high as 50 or 60 yuan per picul of land. The ordinary rental yield accounted for about 50% of the harvest, and there was always the risk of changing tenants. Since the Red Disaster, the price of land has fallen by about 100 yuan, and the deposit money has fallen to more than 10 yuan. The rental yield has also been reduced slightly, and the lease term is longer. If the tenant withdraws, it is mostly proposed by the tenant. If it is proposed by the landlord, in addition to returning the deposit money, a small amount of compensation must be given. Among the farmers in the county, self-cultivating farmers and semi-self-cultivating farmers each account for 20%, and tenant farmers account for 60%. The area of land cultivated by self-cultivating farmers accounts for 15%, and the area of land cultivated by tenant farmers accounts for 85%. In good years, it is only enough to eat, and in normal and famine years, it is necessary to rely on imports from Liu'an and Shucheng.

Tea is the main product, with an annual output of more than 10,000 catties, worth more than 200,000 yuan. The so-called Songluo tea has a rich fragrance and is as famous as Hugiu tea in Wu. The next is bamboo and wood, with an annual output of more than 300,000 plants, worth more than 50,000 yuan. Poria cocos is more than 1,000 piculs, worth more than 20,000 yuan. Broomcorn is more than 200,000 bundles, worth more than 70,000 yuan.

The large groups of bandits in the entire territory have indeed been wiped out, but scattered bandits still rob homes and disturb the people from time to time. The security team has only four platoons, which is very difficult to defend everywhere. The county government has specially formulated twenty articles of the "United Village Anti-Bandit Outline" and ordered it to be issued to the chiefs of each district for compliance. The method is roughly that each bao sends ten strong men every day to form a police team, who are trained in rotation, and gather at 5:00 pm to take on patrol, sentry, reconnaissance, search, and all alert matters. The amount of work is changed every day to avoid delaying farming time, and they rotate in shifts to avoid partial labor. Patrols must strike wooden clappers to correspond to the clapper sounds of other baos. In case of a bandit alert, two shots are fired from a musket to seek assistance. It is said that since the implementation, the cases of "touching melons" and the fear of the wind have begun to decrease day by day.

Songjiang

News of Zhang Huaixi's Calligraphy and Painting Exhibition

Calligrapher and painter Zhang Huaixi of this county is the son of the late famous calligrapher Mr. Shigong. His calligraphy is vigorous and elegant, and he has the spirit of his father. His paintings are exquisite and deeply imbued with the charm of Nantian. He previously held an exhibition at Longtan School. Now, he will hold a second exhibition of his recent works at Xidu School outside the West Gate on the morning of the 31st, to seek comments from the people of Songjiang. It also coincides with the tenth anniversary of the school, and it is expected to be a grand occasion.

Qu Family Robbery Case is Incorrect

The rumor of a robbery at the Qu residence in Xiayang, east of the Ta Bridge outside the West Gate, which was reported the day before yesterday, has been thoroughly investigated and found to be completely fictitious. Not only have the neighboring residences heard nothing about it, but even the servants of the Qu residence are unaware. It is likely that someone dissatisfied with the Qu family fabricated this rumor.

Caojing Anti-Smuggling Team Rescues Hostages

The Anti-Smuggling Camp of Five Prefectures in Jiangsu Province has a detachment stationed in Caojing. Recently, according to reports, hostages were hidden in a certain village more than ten miles from Caojing. The detachment was immediately dispatched to the address to arrest them. On the afternoon of the 28th, two male hostages, one year old and nine years old, with hair an inch long, were rescued. They had been held captive for a long time. The hostage taker was captured and, after interrogation, was found to be from Jiashan. According to the hostage taker, there were still places where hostages were hidden. Another hostage and hostage takers were rescued. All were Jiashan kidnapping cases and are currently under interrogation.

Qingpu

Fire at Fangjia Yao Town

Fangjia Yao Town in the twelfth district of this county caught fire in a rice mill south of the Kongxiang Bridge in Gou City at about 2:00 pm the day before yesterday. The fire was blazing and extremely fierce, making it impossible for firefighters to approach and put it out. In less than an hour, more than 30 factory buildings, more than 200 piculs of white rice, and more than 20 coffins, large and small, in the adjacent Pungongtai shop were completely burned down. The total loss is estimated to be more than 10,000 yuan.

Wuxi

County-wide Clean-up Campaign

Police Chief Li Wengong, because the 29th was the date stipulated by the Jiangsu Provincial Government for the general clean-up, specially convened a discussion meeting of the heads of the urban district branches, section chiefs, and superintendents the day before yesterday, and decided to gather at the headquarters at 9:00 am on the 29th and set off to clean up the streets at 10:00 am. At 10:00 am yesterday, Chief Li personally supervised the heads of each branch, section chiefs, section members, superintendents, service personnel, police officers, sanitation police, and river cleaning laborers to set off, holding flags, and held a general clean-up inside and outside the city, and posted slogans to crack down on street vendors along the way.

Inn Manager Sells Enemy Goods

The Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association of this county received a secret report yesterday that Yang Rongxiang, the manager of the Xin Inn on the road, was selling Japanese-made electric light bulbs. Please send someone to check it immediately. After receiving the report, the association immediately sent inspectors to conduct the inspection. They found 91 suspected enemy-made electric light bulbs of various brands in the manager's room of the inn, and immediately took them all to the association for sealing and storage, pending verification.

Jiangyin

New County Magistrate to Arrive in Cheng on Schedule

Ruan Kaikei, the county magistrate of this county, was ordered to be transferred to the province. The vacancy was filled by Bao Sixin, a qualified county magistrate appointed by the province. Bao has arrived in the province and decided to arrive in Cheng on January 9 next year to take office. County Magistrate Ruan sent his family back to his hometown of Jinshan on the 27th. In the evening, he invited his subordinates to a meal at the county government and instructed the sections to prepare for the handover.

Nantong

Investigating Kidnappers from Shanghai

Recently, the kidnappers in Shanghai are fleeing to Nantong due to the urgent capture. Some are even using sand boats to hide hostages in remote ports along the river. In recent days, many detectives from Shanghai have come to Nantong to investigate and arrest kidnappers. Patrol boats have been dispatched by the Third District of the Provincial Water Police along the river to pay attention to the investigation.

Jiashan

Bandits Plan to Rob Hongxi Town

Hongjiatan Town in this county is located in a water town and is famous for its kiln industry. In the autumn of 1928, the town was robbed by a joint force of Jiangbei, Henan, and Pudong gangs, and many hostages were kidnapped. The town's commerce has fallen into ruin. Unexpectedly, in the midst of devastation, there are rumors that the three gangs will rob the entire town again. On the 24th, Ye, the squad leader of the town's security corps, and Li, the kiln owner, each received threatening letters from Shanghai, stating that the brothers of the three gangs had suffered in the past and were now coming for revenge. Please prepare 3,000 yuan in silver dollars and send someone to Shanghai on the early train to Hangzhou to negotiate, otherwise they will rob the entire town immediately. Squad Leader Ye immediately submitted the original letter to the county government and added strong troops to strictly defend.

Changshu

A Bandit Captured in the Donglai Robbery Case

Donglai Town in the Fourth District was robbed by seventy or eighty pirates on the night of the 27th. All shops and residents were spared. All the circumstances have been recorded and reported. After the incident, Wang Kunshan, the captain of the county police team, took a steamship to conduct a reconnaissance on the 28th and returned to the city at 12:00 am. According to the investigation, there were more than sixty bandits who arrived in the town one after another, and it was not a day. They used four-inch long white cloth as a sign. The day before, they had first gone to the water police station to investigate their strength. As a result, the captain, Li Yinqing, was bound by the bandits, and all the weapons were taken away. Then they went to rob separately. That night, three guests from other provinces suddenly asked to stay overnight in Xin Zhuang Port. Because they were suspicious, one person was arrested, and two escaped. One of them, Li Songjiu, from Nantong, was a tailor. He did not admit to being a thief. Because the police suspected him of being involved, they took him to the bureau and sent him to the county for interrogation on the 29th.

The Haiguan, Haihui, and Haiping Patrol Ships Hold Launching Ceremony Yesterday

Launched by Ms. Bema

The fourth and fifth patrol ships, Haihui and Haiping, built by the Jiangnan Shipyard for the Jianghai Customs, were launched one after another yesterday morning in the drizzle. The launching was done by Ms. Bema, the niece of the Naval Tax Commissioner. They are scheduled to be completed in February next year. The details are as follows:

Arrangement of the Ceremony Platform: A rectangular wooden platform about seven feet high, forty feet long, and twenty feet wide was built in front of the two patrol ships, surrounded by national flags and covered with oilcloth. The Qing Tian Bai Ri Party and National Flags were hung before and after the two ships. The bow of the ship was wrapped with a champagne bottle tied with five-colored silk. At the bottom of the platform ladder, soldiers from the Naval Guard Battalion maintained order.

Cruiser of the Jianghai Customs

Guests Attending: Those who attended yesterday included Mr. Chen Shaokuan, director of the shipyard, represented by Deputy Director Chen Zaofan, Mr. Merlo, the Inspector General of Customs, and his wife, Mr. Maogen, the chief engineer of the shipyard, and his wife, the launcher, Ms. BullmoreSirMaze, CaptHillmau, CaotPrichasdCaptSafel, CaptYuan, CaptJohns, the director and deputy director of the shipyard's business department, Yu Jianfu and Ye Fangzhi, the chief of the material section, Liang Xunying, and students and instructors from the Customs Tax School, etc.

Grand Launch: At 11:15 am, the Haihui ship was launched first. Ms. Bema held a bunch of fresh flowers in her left hand and a champagne bottle with five-colored silk in her right hand, aimed at the bow of the ship, and threw it forcefully. With a bang, it hit the bow of the ship right in the center, and champagne splashed everywhere. The ship then entered the Huangpu River amid cheers and applause and was towed to the shipyard's pier by a small tugboat to dock. At 11:30 am, the Haiping ship was launched by Ms. Bema in the same way, declaring the ceremony a success.

Director's Speech: After the launching, Mr. Chen Zaofan led the Chinese and foreign guests to the shipyard's restaurant for refreshments. Mr. Chen delivered a speech, saying that today is the launching ceremony of the Haihui and Haiping patrol ships, and he was honored to have Mr. Mei, the Inspector General of Customs, and all the Chinese and foreign guests take the time to attend, and he was even more grateful to Ms. Bema for performing the launching ceremony. The two ships are the fourth and fifth ships built by the shipyard for the Customs. Now that they have been launched, they will be completed soon. In the future, they will be able to fulfill their mission of hunting pirates and protecting tax revenue. After Mr. Chen's speech, he raised his glass to Mr. Mei, the Inspector General of Customs, and all the guests to wish each other health. Then Mr. Mei, the Inspector General of Customs, replied.

Full Ship Structure: According to the person in charge of the shipyard, the two patrol ships have a displacement of 395 tons, a length of 135 feet, a width of 24 feet, a depth of 15 feet, a draft of 9 feet, and a speed of 12 nautical miles per hour. They are scheduled to be completed in February next spring. After the two ships were launched, Deputy Director Chen telegraphed Mr. Chen Shaokuan, the Minister of the Navy, in Beijing to report. Mr. Chen also presented Ms. Bema, who launched the bottle, with a lacquer Buddha statue from Fujian Province as a souvenir.

Five Bureaus of the Municipal Government Have Started Working During the Relocation

The Mayor's Office and the Secretary-General's Office

Still Need to Wait Until Tomorrow to Move

Since the Municipal Government and its subordinate offices began to move to the new building in the city center on the 25th of this month, except for the Secretariat and the Land Bureau, which have not been able to complete the move, the others have all started working in the new building in the city center. The details are as follows:

Five Bureaus Started Working: The four bureaus of public works, social affairs, education, and health have all been arranged in the new building and officially started working yesterday. A part of the Land Bureau has also moved into the new building. The three bureaus of social affairs, education, and health are working in the new building on the left side of the municipal government, and the two bureaus of land and public works are working in the new building on the right side. The houses of each bureau are still spacious and connected together, which will be convenient for future work.

The Secretariat Will Be Completed Today: The Municipal Government Secretariat also started moving on the 28th. Opening Ceremony on New Year's Day: The Municipal Government has now decided to hold the opening ceremony on New Year's Day and ordered all staff to attend. The Mayor will host a banquet for the Municipal Government colleagues on that day, but will not invite guests.

After the Arrest of Jin Xi, Public Outrage Intensifies, Resorting to International Appeal

Requesting the World Human Rights Council to Uphold Justice

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, various local legal entities, such as the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, the French Concession Chinese Ratepayers Association, the Lawyers Association, the General Labor Union, and the Citizens' United Association, all believe that since Jin Xi has proven his naturalization as a Chinese citizen, he should be protected by Chinese law. Moreover, he has resided in the French Concession for five or six years. The French Consulate, in collusion with the Japanese police, illegally arrested him. Despite serious protests from the Municipal Government and various legal entities, he has not been released for over a month, causing deep indignation. It is expected that a Jin Xi Relief Organization will be formed soon to jointly telegraph the major powers, requesting a public trial. Yesterday, Chen Yang, the representative of Jin Xi's family, told a reporter from Xin Sheng News Agency that the case of Jin Xi's illegal arrest by the Japanese Consulate has drawn nationwide attention. Various local legal entities deeply feel that this matter harms national sovereignty, and they are able to speak out righteously and strive vigorously, which is highly admirable. However, the Japanese Consulate disregards justice and, despite loud appeals and serious protests, remains indifferent, delaying and procrastinating. With such prolonged detention, Mr. Jin's life is in real danger. Therefore, the family, in addition to requesting the Municipal Government and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to lodge serious protests simultaneously, sees no other recourse. They recently sent a letter to various local legal entities, soliciting methods for providing assistance. In recent days, they have received replies from various legal entities, all willing to join in forming a powerful organization to serve as a backing for the government. They will also telegraph the Paris World Human Rights Protection League, hoping that it will use its great authority to protect human rights, rise up and protest, and promote international attention. They believe that the ultimate truth and falsehood will be subject to public opinion.

China National Aviation Corporation's Plan to Develop National Civil Aviation

Completing Three Major Trunk Lines This Year

Cultivating Domestic Aviation Talent

Shanghai Times News Agency, Shanghai: Since the China National Aviation Corporation (CNAC) has completed the Shanghai-Ping (Beijing), Shanghai-Rong (Chengdu), and Shanghai-Yue (Guangdong) trunk lines one after another, it has recently begun to develop southwestern routes. If the test flights are successful, regular flights will be officially launched. Yesterday, the Shanghai Times reporter visited Mr. Dai Siji, the general manager of CNAC, and asked him to provide detailed information about the future development plan of civil aviation in China. The details are recorded as follows:

Completion of Three Major Trunk Lines: According to Mr. Dai, CNAC has been in operation for three years and has been fully committed to completing the three major trunk lines during this time. The Shanghai-Ping line was launched on January 10th this year, the Yu-Rong line on November 11th this year, and the Shanghai-Yue line on October 24th this year. From then on, the north, south, east, and west will be connected, marking the success of the first phase of the company's development.

Overview of This Year's Business: Regarding the company's business situation, compared to December last year and the same month this year, passenger ticket revenue last year was over 20,000 yuan, and this year it has doubled to about 40,000 yuan. In terms of mail, it was over 40,000 yuan last year and has increased to over 70,000 yuan this year, also a significant improvement. He also showed various statistics from January to the end of November of the 22nd year: (1) The number of passengers was 2,349. (2) The mail carried was 40,767 kilograms. (3) The number of miles flown was 571,912.

Cultivating Aviation Talent: Mr. Dai continued, "When our company first started, we hired many foreign personnel due to the lack of domestic talent. Now, Chinese people are also capable of doing the job. Currently, wireless radio and aircraft repair technicians are all Chinese. The Sino-American contract only lasts for ten years, so cultivating aviation talent is something we cannot delay. Our company has already paid active attention to this."

Expanding Airport Facilities: The Longhua Airport was originally planned to have two runways. One has already been completed, and the second has been under construction for a long time and will be completed soon. This type of new-style airport is rare in the country. New sheds will be built next spring to make it complete.

Developing Southwestern Routes: Mr. Dai concluded, "The current test flights to the southwest are in response to the needs of transportation in the southwest. At the same time, the Yunnan Provincial Government also expressed its approval. Therefore, our company is actively preparing. It was originally scheduled to fly from Hankou the day before yesterday, but the fog was heavy in the Changsha area, so it could not take off as scheduled. It was still raining yesterday, so it did not fly. Once the test flight is successful, the scheduled flight will be launched."

The "Yuji" That Ran Aground at Dongguashan is Safe and Will Return

Expected to Arrive in Shanghai Soon

The Losses Are Quite Significant

The "Yuji" steamer of the Yu Da Company ran aground at Dongguashan near Wenzhou. The company and the Lianbao Insurance Company immediately dispatched the Sanjiang steamer, carrying engineers, equipment, and materials, to provide rescue. After many days of construction, a telegram was received yesterday stating that the ship has been rescued and will soon return to Shanghai. The details are recorded as follows:

Repairing the Holes: The "Yuji" steamer ran aground in the area of the first and second holds. The damage was inspected by the divers brought by the Sanjiang steamer, and it was found that there were only two holes, which were not large and easy to repair. The engineers who came along temporarily filled and repaired the two holes in the bottom of the ship with cement, wood panels, and rubber. Fortunately, the engine room and the rear hold were undamaged, making the rescue easier.

Abandoning the Cargo: The first and second holds were flooded to a depth of 15 feet at the time, and the fruit stored in the holds was rotten and damaged. In order to carry out the ship rescue work, the shipping company and the insurance company decided to abandon the damaged cargo in those two holds. The passengers had consulted with the insurance company insuring the cargo about this matter. It is now learned that the damaged cargo in the first and second holds has been removed. In recent days, the workers transported there have used pumps to remove the accumulated water from the two holds, allowing the hull to float to the surface of the sea, and then sailed away from the shoal with the tide.

The Ship is Safe: It has been 12 days since the "Yuji" steamer ran aground. Yesterday, the company in Shanghai received news that the rescue work of the "Yuji" steamer has been completed. It is expected that it can sail out of the Dongguashan shoal today. The internal engine and machinery are all in good condition. The ship, after sailing out of the shoal, plans to stop temporarily at Ruian near Wenzhou for inspection of the hull to ensure safe navigation, and then sail to Shanghai. The cargo in the third and fourth holds of the ship has not been damaged.

Major Repairs in Shanghai: According to company insiders, the "Yuji" steamer can arrive in Shanghai within three days. After arriving in Shanghai, the cargo will be unloaded and major repairs will be carried out in the dock. The reason for the ship's grounding this time was mainly because the captain changed the route to the inner circle during the voyage, and the wind and waves were huge near the Dongguashan sea area, causing it to be forced to the rocks and hit them. Fortunately, the passengers and crew were unharmed, and the ship was able to escape danger. However, the delay in the voyage, the damage to the goods, the dispatch of ships for rescue, and the employment of technicians have resulted in significant losses.

International Trade Bureau Convenes Egg Merchants' Meeting Yesterday

Discussing Countermeasures Against France's Increase in Egg Tax

Resolved to Request the Ministry of Finance to Reduce Egg Export Tax

The International Trade Bureau received instructions from the Ministry of Industry stating that France's increase in the license tax for egg imports and restrictions on import quantities have a significant impact on China's egg industry. The bureau was ordered to convene local egg merchants to discuss remedial measures. Therefore, yesterday at 3:00 PM, the bureau convened various egg merchants for a meeting in the conference room of the bureau. More than ten representatives, including those from Maochangli and Huan, attended. Various countermeasures were resolved. The details of the meeting are recorded as follows:

Attendees: The representatives who attended yesterday were Zheng Jiying (Lihuan), Shi Yingke, Lin Haijin, Chen Qingcheng (Central Refrigeration Factory), Pan Younian, Wang Lizhuan, Wang Xifan (Xiji), Zheng Yuanxing (Maochang), Cui Lianggong (Egg Industry Association), Man Cai (Peiji), Bao Siting, Mai Su, Sha Bo, and Dang Youjize, chaired by Ji Zequan.

Chairman's Report: After the ceremony, the chairman gave a brief report, stating that the position of China's egg exports is extremely important. It ranked third in 1930, fourth in 1931, and third again in 1932. Exports to France account for 4% of egg exports, with frozen eggs being the most and fresh eggs being very few. It was estimated that 15,027 piculs were exported in 1912, 21,884 piculs in 1922, and 33,057 piculs in 1932. The number of exports has gradually increased, but in the fourth quarter of 1933, France limited the amount that China could export to 142.5 tons, equivalent to 2,394 piculs. According to this calculation, it is about 9,576 piculs per year, which is too different from the number of exports from China in previous years. This time, France has increased the import license tax for frozen eggs to 4 francs and 60 centimes per net kilogram, which is almost 100% of the value. Compared with the fresh egg tax (1 franc and 50 centimes per net kilogram), the fresh egg tax is only one-third of the frozen egg tax. This modification of the import restriction quantity takes the purchase of French goods by various countries as the standard. The imposition of frozen egg tax directly hits China's export trade and indirectly affects the rural economy. Countries are promoting the chicken raising industry, and egg production can gradually be self-sufficient. They are all adopting tariff protection policies, increasing egg import taxes, and restricting import quantities.

Resolutions: In addition to the following three points, the egg merchants proposed yesterday that the ice egg industry and the egg industry association will hold another meeting to submit their opinions to the International Trade Bureau for implementation by the Ministry of Industry. (1) (Countermeasures) France has increased import taxes on egg exports from our country and restricted the amount of our country's exports. It is requested that our government take countermeasures by increasing the import tax on French goods entering China, or restricting them by a corresponding amount. (2) (Method of Exchange of Equivalent Goods) The goods imported from France to our country are mostly cosmetics and consumer goods, which are light in weight and have high profits. The goods imported from our country to France are mostly raw materials or agricultural products, which are heavy in weight and have low profits. If France increases taxes on agricultural products imported from our country, and our country only increases taxes on consumer goods imported from that country, the advantages and disadvantages are very different in comparison. Therefore, our country should use the principle of increasing tax rates on equivalent items. (3) Request the Ministry of Industry to consult the Ministry of Finance to reduce egg export taxes in order to ease the burden on egg merchants.

Ministry of Industry Instructions: The International Trade Bureau received instructions from the Ministry of Industry, the original text of which is as follows: Approved the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' advice, according to the French Embassy's presentation, requesting the government to increase the import license tax for frozen eggs and modify the import restriction quantity, advise for verification and handling, etc., and attach a copy of the original letter from the French Frozen Egg Importers Association and a copy of the French agricultural product import table to the ministry. After reviewing the attached original letter, it requested that efforts be made to negotiate with the French government to increase the restriction quantity and to assist in negotiating a reduction in the frozen egg import license tax. This case is implemented uniformly by the French government to all countries, based on the same principles for distribution. However, the French government has changed the collection of the import license tax for frozen eggs, which is almost 100% of the value. Compared with the fresh egg license tax, the fresh egg tax is only one-third of the frozen egg tax. And our country exports the most frozen eggs to France, and very few fresh eggs. Therefore, this change in the license tax is the most unfavorable to our country's egg export industry. According to last year's data, the quantity of eggs exported by our country to France only accounted for 4% of the total egg exports. Now the French government has increased the license tax and will modify the import restriction quantity. Our country's egg industry urgently needs to improve quality, reduce costs, and improve sales methods in order to develop. In addition to separately advising the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of Finance to discuss this matter, the attached letters and the original attachments, as well as a translation of the letter from the French Chamber of Commerce and a document from our ministry advising the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of Finance, are hereby copied to you. Please carefully plan a remedial plan and convene egg merchants to discuss in detail, sign and express your opinions, and submit them together for verification and handling.

Labor-Management Dispute at Sanyou Industrial Society Resolved

Both Parties Signed a Peace Treaty at the Cotton Control Association Yesterday

Dagon News Agency reported that the case of Sanyou Industrial Society and the Shanghai Seventh District Cotton Weaving Industry Union, which involved dismissal disputes and litigation enforcement, has lasted for two years. The targets of the dispute between the two parties are different, and there is no proper solution. The Cotton Control Association of the National Economic Commission believes that with the dumping of foreign goods and the decline of domestic industries, labor and management should sincerely help each other. If the case continues to be entangled in litigation, neither party will benefit. Therefore, the association appointed its member Du Junsheng to mediate. Mr. Du was well aware of the difficulties of both parties, and the plan he proposed was very pertinent. After several contacts, the result was very satisfactory. Yesterday (December 29th) at 4:00 PM, a reconciliation contract was signed in the office of the Cotton Control Association. Gong Yuting, Zhang Yihai, and Bao Boyi from the labor side, Cen Zihou, Ji Jiannan from the capital side, as well as lawyers and Mr. Du Yuesheng and Chen Guangfu, all signed in order. All the rights of the labor side to the right to resume work, food allowance, and dismissal fees under the original contract as stated in the decision of the Shanghai Labor-Management Arbitration Committee on September 1, 1931, are waived. The spirit and form of the labor side's willingness to show consideration for the capital side to give up vested rights are consistent. During the meeting, the reconciliation method previously agreed upon was followed to sign a peace treaty and declare the completion of the resolution. After the signing of this document, the two parties will separately file statements to withdraw all litigation cases. The dispute that had been delayed for two years has now come to a complete and satisfactory end.
