Commentary

Lodging a Protest to Them

— Chuan Yi Zhi

This month on the Xth, this newspaper reported: According to the International Trade Bureau's announced figures on the prices of imported perfumes and cosmetics from January to October of this year, the total has reached 1,398,664 yuan... Some people have based on this point, published articles, severely scolding women. In fact, this mere million-plus yuan consumption, aside from some high-class prostitutes who regard perfume and cosmetics as a "commodity" and an unavoidable part of their costs, isn't it mostly the idle class of young mistresses and young ladies helping their husbands or fathers spend their excess money on these consumables? The majority of women have rarely seen them spend a few dollars to buy one or two kinds of imported perfumes and cosmetics! Moreover, they—young mistresses, young ladies—have their own unspoken reasons for using them, as they want to please their husbands or lovers!

On June 13th of this year, a certain newspaper reported a Reuters dispatch from London: The daily cost of grooming for women in the United States exceeds 300,000 pounds sterling, totaling over 11,200,000 pounds sterling annually... This shows that women—excluding those unworthy of being called wives and misses—are wholly dependent on grooming for their livelihood, and it seems that men produce while women consume, also a natural law; no wonder the American government recognizes that wives should enjoy a large portion of their husband's wages, so from July 1st, 6/5 of the wages of the 200,000 water conservancy workers recruited by the government will be directly mailed to their wives or families (see the National News Agency's Washington dispatch on June 27th). If this is the case in America, how can China be an exception?

Besides, using perfumes and cosmetics requires money and effort, and the idle class of young mistresses and young ladies have plenty of money and time. I remember the jest of Li Yingbi, Qing Hefu, and the monk of Mount Fu; "Once a carpenter mistakenly hooked onto the underworld, and Yama ordered the original hooker to send him back, but the original hooker demanded a bribe and refused to go. The carpenter had nothing to give, so he thought of his former master, Shen Wansan, the richest man in his lifetime, and asked him for a loan. Wansan said: 'You are a carpenter, and you once helped me into my coffin, did you ever see me carry anything with me?'" Money is only a kind of collateral in the trading fields after the "midday market" system was overthrown. We are born naked and die in all kinds of ways, and we have never been buried with a hundred thousand in our belts. They have this "heroic" state of mind and this "free and untrammeled" view of life, and they have never suffered hardships to earn their living. My friend T is studying the manufacture of Nail Polish, and I asked him what use this has in life, and he said with a smile, "Just finding something for them to relax with!" They already have sufficient grooming skills, so if they don't spray perfume or apply cosmetics, what would you have them do?

Therefore, from now on, if anyone discusses Chinese modern women in the manner that Dracula discussed Chinese women, I will lodge a protest to them.

A Record of a Certain Driver's Affair

— Feng

The "certain driver" mentioned here is a train driver on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway. He was a naturally kind person, and his service experience and driving skills were also very adequate because railway drivers all started as stokers. However, he killed three people in a row at the same location within the same year, which almost drove him insane. Although the railway had already given him a dismissal, he still felt extremely uneasy and often beat his chest and grieved endlessly. However, this is a very bizarre story. How could he kill three people in a row at the same location? So I went to visit him and got to the bottom of this matter.

At the beginning of the year, he was assigned to be the driver of a certain train, but he suddenly fell ill. After a delay of three days, on the fourth day, he was driving a passenger train about fifty or sixty yards long from Shanghai North Station to Nanjing. When the train reached the area between two stations, he suddenly saw a person walking on the tracks ahead. So he sounded the steam whistle as a warning, assuming that this person would immediately move aside. Unexpectedly, the person ahead seemed to be deaf and continued to walk along the tracks. As the distance narrowed, he became too anxious to brake and desperately sounded the steam whistle, but the person never moved and was crushed into three pieces under the wheels. Afterward, the train staff all testified on his behalf, proving that he had indeed frantically sounded the steam whistle and had not neglected his duty. As a result, he only received a minor penalty.

Four or five months passed, and he gradually forgot about this incident. One midday, he was driving a passenger train again, passing between the two stations, and when he arrived at the same location where the accident had happened last time, he suddenly saw a figure swaying in the distance ahead. He took precautions and pulled the long steam whistle, continuously pulling it for about two minutes. Looking ahead again, the shadow of the person was particularly clear. So he hurriedly braked and notified the stoker to help sound the steam whistle frantically. Unexpectedly, this person was standing there as if nailed to the spot and did not move, and the train could not stop immediately, so the second tragedy occurred. He simply didn't dare to get out of the train to look. He felt that this matter was too strange. He hid in the driver's compartment and trembled as much as possible, and could no longer continue to drive the train forward. This time he was sick for half a month and received a major demerit. But soon he returned to work. Of course, he could not be transferred to another position and was still a driver. On one occasion, he was driving the overnight train, and at eight or nine o'clock in the morning, he arrived again between the two stations. In the bright sunlight, he suddenly saw a person running from the side of the road onto the tracks as if he were crazy. This time, his first action was to brake, desperately braking, regardless of the mechanics, but that person rushed towards the train, making him so frightened that he used one hand to pull the steam whistle and the other to cover his eyes, not daring to look ahead again. However, when the train stopped, an incomplete corpse had been added under the wheels. The strangest thing was that it was still in the same place as the previous two accidents, at most only a few yards apart.

Cold Night

— Drunken Bamboo

A misty drizzle drifts down in gusts. The streetlamp on the corner casts a dim, green glow. The biting northwest wind loves to be close to the poor, avoiding the wealthy in their thick fur coats. Now and then, the clang of a streetcar bell punctuates the desolate cold night.

By this time, the shops on both sides of the road are likely closed, due to the cold weather and slow business. The shop assistants, who have worked hard all day, spread out their bedding and burrow into their quilts – their paradise. Before long, loud snores join the sound of the wind outside, creating a symphony.

The snoring travels with the wind to the ears of the apprentice at the fruit stand across the street, causing him to shrink his neck. He thinks how carefree the shop assistants are, already asleep, warm and cozy. He, on the other hand, has to endure the wind every day until past midnight. Thinking this, he looks up at the boss. The boss seems to understand his meaning and glances around softly. He says, "Let's pack up!" He then looks at the money box and shakes his head.

The apprentice could not have wished more for these words! Instantly, the biting north wind transforms into a gentle spring breeze. He happily rushes to pack up the stall and follows the boss home to sleep.

At this moment, on the street corner, a homeless person, still has no place to rest despite it being eleven o'clock on a cold night. Seeing the fruit stand close, he sighs in disappointment! He thinks that no matter how late, they have a master to provide them lodging. But he, like a bird that has lost its forest, has nowhere to settle. He feels in his pocket and finds only a dozen or so copper coins, ending all fantasies of a warm bed. He resents the tall foreign buildings on both sides, unable to accommodate his small body. The world is so unfair! He walks on, filled with resentment, when suddenly he hears laughter from upstairs, coming from behind a green window shade. He looks up and sees two figures slowly, slowly, drawing closer until suddenly! They embrace. After a long while, another chuckle, and then they are two shadows again... The "wanderer" is stunned! It is as if he once had a similar experience in his own mind... He wants to shout to those behind the curtain, telling them not to indulge in this rosy dream, because behind every dream is the dim light like tonight and the struggle to survive in the northwest wind. But he lacks the courage, because the world is inherently unequal; some dream, and some wander.

The Northeast Fourth Company Commander

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Twenty-One: Murmurs by the Lamp, Earnest Advice to a Weak Daughter; A Stroll in the Mountains, Cold Eyes Observing Heroes

Madam Jiang pushed the small kerosene lamp on the table to the side, letting Guizhi have more light. She held the fabric with both hands and looked at Guizhi for a long while, smiling faintly: "People say, read the news, read the news. You found this old newspaper to read. This isn't reading news, it's reading old news. How many characters do you even know? And you're reading a newspaper!" Guizhi said, "This is a newspaper that old master found, Xiao Lin brought it over. I was bored, so I read it to pass the time. I read the parts I know, and I don't read the parts I don't know." Madam Jiang said, "Why would Xiao Lin bring you a newspaper for no reason?" Guizhi didn't raise her head, but slightly lifted her eyelids and smiled at her mother: "It's not hard to understand, it's just to let me see the news on the newspaper, saying that the area outside the pass is now peaceful." Madam Jiang, upon hearing this, kept her hands on her lap and nodded slightly, expressing her approval. She then said, "People like Old Master Zhao are truly loving to their children. Now that we're related, just for the old man's good intentions, we should treat him well. As the saying goes, one good turn deserves another." Guizhi put her hand on the newspaper, looked at her mother, and said, "What do you mean by that? I don't understand." Although she said this, her eyes remained on the newspaper, not paying attention to her mother. Madam Jiang raised her head slightly and sighed. As she sighed, her eyes stopped looking at her daughter and instead looked at the kerosene lamp shade. After a while, she said to herself, "There are too many idle people on Haidian Street, who stir up trouble for no reason, wanting to talk about the East family's long suits and the West family's short suits. If your family has any shortcomings, then that's it, they'll add some oil and salt, and the joke will be even bigger. As the saying goes: There's a lot of gossip at a widow's door. I'm a widow, and my daughter is an only child, sigh! We must be careful in everything. Although it's the age of reform, you still have to see what it is. For women, talking about the three obediences and four virtues is acceptable anywhere." (281)

Artistic Traces

Memories of a Trip to Fujian (Part 2)

— SY

Fuzhou lacquerware is exquisite and delicate, famous throughout the provinces, but the price is very expensive. When people from other provinces go to buy it, they often have to pay more than double. In terms of food, Fujian cuisine is also known for being elaborate, but the prices are not cheaper than those in Shanghai's Fujian restaurants. The rice cooked in homes and restaurants here is almost like pearls, with each grain separate and completely lacking stickiness. We are really not used to eating this kind of rice. It is said that when they cook rice, after the rice is put into the pot, once the water boils, they pour out or discard the sticky rice water, or it is bought by laundries to use for washing clothes. So the rice is inedible, but the washed clothes are particularly well cared for.

The water used for bathing in Fuzhou is entirely from hot springs, like Tangshan in Nanjing. The water has a slight sulfur smell, which is very beneficial to people's health. Therefore, the bathhouses here are also very famous. There is a road in the city called Hot Spring Road, where the most hot spring bathhouses in Fuzhou are located. The most modern one is the Mingyuan Bathhouse of the Baihe Company. Each bath has a room, or two baths share a room. Both men and women can go, but women are separated and have female attendants to greet them. Outside the bathhouse rooms, there is a lotus pond, rockeries, and trees. The scenery is extremely serene and beautiful.

Small West Lake is near the West Gate. There are not many trees, but there is a teahouse that can accommodate ten people for resting. More than a dozen small boats are placed in the center of the lake. As the sun sets, pairs of lovers sit side by side in the boats, drifting on the lake. There is not much else to describe. Compared to West Lake in Hangzhou, it is worlds apart.

About thirty li from the provincial capital is Drum Mountain, which is extremely famous in Fuzhou. However, it is impossible to return on the same day. You need to stay on the mountain for at least one day. When we went, there were six men and two women. We hired two cars and sped to the foot of the mountain. Everyone bravely started climbing the mountain, but before reaching halfway, most of them were unable to walk. So, they switched to shoulder carriers and continued their efforts. Unexpectedly, the weather turned bad, and it started to drizzle. In an instant, it rained harder and harder. At this time, we were halfway up the mountain, and we could not retreat. We had no choice but to be soaked by the rain. So, when we reached the mountain, we were all like drowned chickens. There is a very large temple on the mountain, but unfortunately, I have forgotten its name at this moment. When we arrived, many monks were performing Buddhist rituals. Listening to the sounds of the sutras, everyone suddenly had some great insights. We all borrowed monk robes from the temple and took a group photo in monk attire. Only the two misses refused to act as nuns temporarily, no matter what. We had no choice but to give up. We stayed overnight in the Mingyue Tower in the temple. In the tower, we discovered two things: a rat as big as a cat and a spider as big as a bowl. When the huge spider was discovered, the two misses screamed in fright. Overnight, we only heard the sound of rain, and the mosquitoes kept us from sleeping soundly. By dawn, the rain had slowed down slightly. We each took a short walk around and went down the mountain to return. It can be said that we came with enthusiasm and returned disappointed. We still did not get to appreciate the famous mountain. When I went to Fuzhou for the second time, I heard that there had been kidnappings at Drum Mountain, so we could not go.

The first time I went, I did not plan to stay long, so after a few days, I returned to Shanghai. The second time, I planned to stay longer, but as soon as I arrived in Fuzhou, the Communists were causing trouble in Yanping, and Fuzhou was very tense. Some of our companions had brought their families, so we were so scared that we had no choice but to run to Hong Kong. At this time, I decided to wait for a ship to Shanghai and temporarily stayed at a friend's house in Cangqian Mountain. After a few days, the Wanxiang of the Sanbei Company arrived. Who knew that when I went to book a room, there were none left. Finally, I managed to get a room with the help of an acquaintance. I even boarded the ship a day in advance to avoid the crowds, but on the small steamboat to Majiang, because the ship was small and the waves were big, and it was getting dark, there was almost a dangerous situation. In the end, we arrived safely at the ship. I slept in the room all night, and at lunchtime the next day, I was carried back to Shanghai by the Wanxiang in the vast sea.

Page 17

Free Talk

From the Jianghu to the Foreign Concession

— Fengzi

The Jianghu is the origin of hermits and chivalrous individuals.

After the change of dynasties, many remnants of the previous dynasty, knowing that the situation was hopeless and that they could no longer serve their masters, attached themselves to elegance and became hermits. Today they write a few poems, tomorrow they fill in a verse, raise caged birds, and plant potted flowers. This one is an "old friend of smoke and mist," and that one is a "wandering man of the Jianghu." Even young men in their twenties, as long as they can hum a few lines, are given the titles of "Taoist" or "Lay Buddhist"; as if they were going to live with smoke and water for the rest of their lives. In reality, they are just residents of the bustling city, spendthrifts of the foreign concession, lacking any real spirit of the Jianghu.

But who dares to say that these are not hermits!

In fact, nowadays, not only hermits need to escape to the foreign concession, but even chivalrous individuals need to leave the Jianghu. There are many heroes in Shanghai who stand up for others. If some girl from the countryside admires the prosperity of the city and comes to Shanghai alone, there are "generous" chivalrous individuals who volunteer to accompany her to see plays, eat snacks, and open a hotel room. In the end, they even "escort the beauty for a thousand miles," escorting her straight into a fiery pit.

If the family sends someone to look for her, then that's even better. Then, another group of chivalrous individuals step forward to help search in different directions; as usual, they always find her, but they can't meet, and some money needs to be used first. Once the money is in hand, they make some excuses, as if "success is just around the corner," or else they "fly away into the sky."

But they may not fly to the Jianghu.

Catching adulterers, fighting brawls, looking for quarrels, and extorting money, these are also the tasks of these chivalrous individuals of the foreign concession.

The foreign concession is naturally lively. Besides hermits and chivalrous individuals, there are also fortune-tellers, magicians, street performers, and peep shows. In the past, they roamed the Jianghu, now they sit in the foreign concession.

It seems that it is much more comfortable here, the Jianghu should be deserted!

"The Reeds are Green, the White Dew is Frost" (Continued)

— Cao Juren

Therefore, the first thing for a poet is to choose an object that can be used to evoke and express emotions. I remember a story in "Dream of the Red Chamber," saying that after Jia Baoyu was beaten by his father, one day, he asked Qingwen to send two old silk handkerchiefs to Lin Daiyu; Qingwen was afraid that Lin Daiyu would be annoyed and refused to send them; Jia Baoyu said: "Don't worry, she will naturally understand." Sure enough, Lin Daiyu understood the meaning of the silk handkerchiefs, and felt intoxicated, and even wrote a few quatrains on them. These two silk handkerchiefs appeared three times in "Dream of the Red Chamber"; until Lin Daiyu was dying, she tore up these two silk handkerchiefs violently, to vent her anger. Private feelings that could not be expressed in thousands of words can be expressed very intimately with just two handkerchiefs, which shows that Jia Baoyu chose them well. It is also said that a certain painter used "Raindrops falling on an empty staircase" as the subject of the painting, "empty staircase" is just an abstract concept, and "drops" is just a concept that is clear in the mind but difficult to paint, making it difficult for people to start. A certain student painted a painting boy, holding an inkstone to catch the dripping water, completely bringing out the theme, which is also a proper selection of materials. In short, emotion is "abstract," and we must express it "concretely." The more vividly it is expressed, the more it can move people. I once saw a work at a photography exhibition with the theme of a water carrier, with vast waves, and distinct human figures. The work was inscribed with the words "A burden of the world on one shoulder," which fully expressed the hardships of the human world, and made people linger for a long time. The poem "The Reeds" has a feeling of helplessness, which makes future generations sigh, doesn't it have the same meaning?

Since ancient times, lyrical poetry should be based on the Xing style; reeds and white dew are just the right representative works. The predecessors said that the Xing style is inevitably close to the mysterious; I think that taking the object that ignites emotions as the beginning of writing can also be said to be close to an objective standard.

You are all studying literature and art, so I will be foolishly presumptuous.

Reading a History of Hungarian Literature

— Yiwu

While casually reading a history of Hungarian literature, I became very interested in three "patriotic poets," including Petőfi.

In the 1850s, the Hungarian people were concerned about the danger facing their nation and suffered from the pain of autocratic oppression, which led to the emergence of patriotic poets. The most outspoken and most supported by the people was Petőfi. Arany was also as famous as him. Reading his allegorical poem "The Shackled Crane" allows one to imagine the poet's environment and the status of his nation at that time. But he was also "fortunate," as Tompa, who was as famous as him and lived in the same era, did not have the freedom to write poetry like that.

Tompa had to write many allegorical poems. He wrote a poem called "Beyond the Crane" in response to "The Shackled Crane." The gist of it is this: "Spring has come, and the crane has returned to its old nest; but crane, you have been deceived, because there is no spring here. Fly back to the happy sky, don't look for our grasslands, our grasslands have turned into cemeteries. Don't stand in our ponds, because the water in the ponds is mixed with human blood. Don't perch on our roof, the roof is full of burnt wood. Go back to the south, because you are happier than us, God gave you two homes, but we only have one, and even that one has been lost. Fly back, and if you meet people who escaped from here earlier, tell them that we are declining, weakening, and disintegrating day by day."

As for Petőfi, he rarely wrote allegorical poems. When the news of the outbreak of the revolution on March 14, 1848, reached the Hungarian capital, causing the cabinet to fall, Petőfi wrote the famous "We, Hungary," and recited it in front of a large crowd on the fifteenth. The last sentence of each chapter of this poem is "We swear, we swear never to be slaves again!" A chorus of voices responded—in today's terms, it's like shouting slogans. After Petőfi finished reciting the poem, the crowd immediately rushed to the printing press, dragged away the censor, and had the poem printed. This was the first poem published without censorship!

How glorious! Patriotic poets, national writers! It turns out that you don't have to rely on the power of the saber to publish your works, which, in my opinion, I always suspect is a lie of literary historians!

Dream

— Li Huiying

Parking his rickshaw by the street and sitting on the footrest to rest, he thought of that matter again.

That matter had been haunting him for more than half a month. Even in his sleep at night, he often woke up in shock. "Five hundred thousand first prize," it was really a great fortune! He wanted to get rich, so he couldn't sleep well, worrying and calculating.

For several days, he really wanted to take a risk and spend two dollars to buy two small strips. The two dollars were what he had secretly saved from pulling rickshaws for several years, hidden in his belt, not even his own wife knew about it. Now, he wanted to use this one-of-a-kind accumulated savings to make a fortune.

"Five hundred thousand, really a great fortune."

He repeated it, but he always lacked the courage, so he still hadn't bought it these days. He understood it very clearly himself; with so many numbers, how could he possibly get lucky? His fate was no good, otherwise he wouldn't have suffered all these years. And he somewhat believed in fate, so the two dollars were kept in his belt and hadn't moved at all.

However, he was conflicted. He also thought: That, isn't it unavoidable to get lucky? Even if he didn't dare to hope for the first prize, the second prize, the third prize, and many small prizes, wouldn't any prize be more than two dollars? As long as he could win, that would be fine. Xiao Liu, who also pulled rickshaws, won twenty dollars last month. You can't say that rickshaw pullers can't win prizes, that they don't have good luck.

Just then, the clerks in a cigarette shop next to where he was parked shouted loudly:

"If you want to get rich, come and buy it, there are only three days left, Aviation Highway Lottery, first prize five hundred thousand, one dollar for a strip!"

In front of the counter, there was a crowd of people, frantically reaching into their pockets, handing over the crisp white dollars without hesitation or stinginess, and then receiving the lottery tickets. They walked away happily as if they had bought treasure. People were so busy buying, as if the fortune was about to leave in a moment. Only at this moment, buying a ticket would make you rich. He was a little flustered, he wanted to do it.

"Leave it to fate!"

Making his final decision, he stood up from the footrest and finally squeezed into the crowd. After a while, when he squeezed out again, two lottery tickets replaced his two banknotes.

"001785"

"467203"

He firmly remembered the numbers on the two lottery tickets. These numbers would follow him into his sleep.

Now that he had spent his only savings for years, in order to make a fortune, he had to put all his hope on expectation. He was looking forward to the twenty-ninth in two days. On that day, a transformation would come to his head, either "sorrow" or "joy."

But at this moment, he was walking with a happy mood, pulling his rickshaw.

Small Notes from a Traveler's Window

— Zhu

18

I have written two articles to record the banning of Su Shi's works. Recently, while reading "Collected Works of Yuan Xiaoxiu," I found another important material. This is what Xiaoxiu said in the "Small Preface to Dragon Lake Remnants":

The writings of Zizhan's life, since the decree from Suzhou, half of them entered the Dragon Palace. The rest of his writings that were hidden in double walls for people after he wrote them by the pond could not be preserved. It was not until the Xuanhe era that a Taoist priest in a memorial pointed to him as Kui Star, and then the ban on Su Shi's writings was lifted.

The strictness of the ban on Su Shi's works at that time was such that it even reached this point. Later, the lifting of the ban, which was based on the Taoist priest's pointing to him as Kui Star, is particularly difficult to believe. Because the resolution of political events will never be so simple.

Two Brothers (74)

— Guy de Maupassant, translated by Li Weike

The egoism in his soul had put on the mask of integrity, and all the disguised and hidden interests were fighting and struggling with each other in his soul. The initial worry gave way to clever reasoning, then reappeared, then disappeared again.

He turned around and sat down, searching for a motive for a decision, a strong excuse to fix his hesitation, to convince his natural honesty. He had raised this question many times: "Since I am this man's son, since I know this and have admitted to being his son, isn't it very natural for me to accept his property?" But this argument could not stop his conscience from saying to him in a low voice, "No."

Suddenly, he thought: "Since I am not the son of the man I used to think was my father, then I can no longer accept anything from him, whether when he is alive or after he is dead. This is neither right nor fair. This property should belong to my brother in the future."

This new way of looking at things made him feel a little relieved, eased his conscience a little, and he returned to the window.

"That's right," he thought, "I should no longer accept the inheritance from the family, I have to give it all to Bill, because I am not his father's son. That's how it should be. Then isn't it right for me to keep my father's property?"

Since he had admitted that he could not use Roland's property, and he had decided to give it up completely, he agreed and allowed himself to keep Maraisa's share, because if he did not accept either share, he would become destitute.

Now that this difficult matter had been resolved, he thought about Bill's problem at home again. How could he get him to leave home? He couldn't think of a feasible way when the whistle of a steamboat entering the dock seemed to give him an answer, suggesting an idea to him.

So he lay down on his bed with his clothes on and dreamed until dawn.

Around nine o'clock, he went out to see if his plan was possible. Later, after running around to several places and visiting a few people, he came to his parents' house. His mother was waiting for him in the room.

"If you didn't come," she said, "I wouldn't dare to go down."

She had just finished speaking when she heard Roland shouting on the stairs:

"Aren't we going to eat today, damn it!"

No one answered, and he grumbled angrily:

"Josephine, damn it! What are you doing?"

The maid's voice came from the basement:

"I'm here, sir, what do you want?"

"Where is madam?"

"Madam and Mr. Zhean are upstairs."

So he raised his head to the upper floor and shouted:

"Louise?"

Roland's mother answered, half-opening the door:

"What's the matter, friend?"

"Aren't we going to eat, damn it!"

"Okay, we're coming."

So she came down, followed by Zhean.

Roland saw the young man and said loudly:

"Oh, you've come! Have you grown tired of your new home?"

"No, father, but I have something to discuss with mother this morning."

Zhean spread out his palms and walked forward. When he felt his hand being held affectionately by the old man, a strange and unexpected emotion made him convulse, the emotion of separation, of no hope of return, of eternal farewell.

Securities

December Government Bond Delivery Proceeds Smoothly

The total delivery amount at the exchange was only 8,700,050

Yesterday was the delivery date for December futures at the Chinese Securities Exchange, and it proceeded very smoothly. The amount was not very large. The total amount was 28,889,000. After deducting the 20,018,500 cleared by the brokers themselves, the amount delivered at the exchange was only 8,700,050. The amount delivered off-exchange could not be verified, but it was rumored to be over 10 million. Four was the number of the firm that most often took delivery. Twenty-one and thirty-two also often delivered bonds. Deliveries came more often from smaller investors. The whole process was full of drama. After the resignation of Finance Minister Song, the bond market became tumultuous. In November, there was hardly a day without storms. On December 1, the lowest price of the reduced military bonds was 51.8 yuan. Compared with the highest price of 65.5 yuan on November 1, the difference was almost 14 yuan. The highest and lowest prices of the salt tax bonds also differed by almost 10 yuan. In between, there were large fluctuations up and down, so most investors made a considerable profit, while speculators were exhausted. The news was often surprising, and those who followed blindly were often misled. After Song resigned and Kong succeeded him, there were initial political rumors, followed by rumors of reorganizing domestic and foreign debts and issuing new government bonds. The resumption of diplomatic relations between the U.S. and Russia and the seriousness of the situation in the Far East also affected the market. In mid-November, the Fujian Incident suddenly broke out, leading to more rumors and war clouds. Bond prices plummeted. Later, the market sentiment was greatly boosted by the neutral stance of the Southwest, and major players bought heavily, causing the market price to recover quickly. Due to the shortage of reduced military bonds, the recovery was the fastest. Currently, the war in Fujian and Zhejiang is becoming increasingly serious. It is believed that the central government will deal with Fujian alone, so there will not be many problems. The bond market may experience another surge. Therefore, trading on the exchange is also extremely active. The total number of futures transactions in December was 51,149,500 yuan. Yarn and Cotton

Record of This Month's Marked Yarn and Cotton Delivery

11,250 bales of yarn, average price 170 yuan

15,500 dan of cotton, average price 39.5 yuan

The December marked yarn started on July 1, with a price of 198.1 yuan, rising slightly to 200.1 yuan. At that time, old cotton was being replaced by new cotton. The U.S. cotton market fluctuated due to the implementation of inflationary policies. Then, sales in the autumn were disappointing, and banditry in Sichuan and Jiangxi was rampant, delaying real demand. As a result, Shanghai's inventory increased daily. There were over 30,000 bales of yarn in warehouses. At the same time, Japanese merchants were dumping in all directions, further impacting Chinese yarn. Although the factories tried to maintain the price, sales decreased overall. Some holders had no way out and had to dump on the futures market. As a result, the southern market gradually declined, breaking the 180 yuan mark. Then, on October 16, the Cotton Industry Control Council was established, which initially stabilized yarn prices and started [to address] yarn inventories [in] yarn and fabric [companies]. The market price was temporarily stabilized, rising slightly to 189 yuan. Unexpectedly, the situation in Zhejiang changed abruptly, and the yarn market suddenly changed with the situation. A bull in a certain factory had no intention of taking delivery and would exceed [a certain amount]. Rumors in the market spread that the Control Council also abandoned its plan to take delivery. Suddenly, like a bolt from the blue, the market crashed like a broken bamboo. The price fell by 6-7 yuan in one day, a situation rare in the past. The market was as chaotic as hemp. The exchange increased the special margin for sellers, reaching a maximum of 60 yuan. The number of times the margin was increased was unprecedented. However, the facts were as such, and the trend was unstoppable. As a result, there was no proper solution. By the beginning of this month, the market atmosphere was the worst since the exchange was established. As sellers were preparing to deliver actual goods, buyers were hesitant due to the worsening environment. Therefore, the lowest price fell below the 70 yuan mark, discovering a new low since the Republic of China. Then, the exchange's shareholders, seeing the bad situation, organized a bull company to buy some of the marked yarn at 170 yuan and prepared to sacrifice and sell it cheaply outside to quickly get rid of this stock from the exchange. As a result, the market temporarily stabilized. On the last day, four rounds were auctioned, all at 170 yuan. In the end, 11,250 bales remained, and the delivery price was averaged at 170 yuan over three days, totaling 1,912,500 yuan. It was heard that the buyers were all bull companies: Yu Da 6,550 bales, Rui Da 1,500 bales, and Yuan Da 1,050 bales. The deliveries were all scattered, with products such as 20-count Ren, Zhong, Long Chuan, and Cai Hua yarn. The broker numbers and brand quantities of the receiving and delivering parties are listed below for reference.

The December Zheng marked cotton started on July 1, with a price of 45.6 yuan. At that time, it was the era of old cotton. The inventory was decreasing daily, which was inversely proportional to yarn. In July and August, the cry for short squeezes was loud. Distant new cotton was also affected, so the cotton price was higher than the yarn price. Later, the news came that our Finance Minister Song Ziwen had signed a loan agreement in the United States to purchase cotton and wheat on credit, causing a shock in the market and a small drop. However, buyers continued to hold tight. Then, on August 8, the U.S. cotton government estimated a bumper harvest, and the price became unstable. At the same time, the price of rice in our country was low, and the new cotton fields increased by one-third, and the rainfall was balanced, so the cotton production looked good. The market price gradually declined, reaching a minimum of 39 yuan. Then, when the new cotton was released, there were claims that the moisture content was too high and the delivery standards were substandard, and the market price rose again to 41.5-6 yuan. By the middle of this month, the effort to maintain the yarn price failed, and the yarn price reached a new low. Factory purchases were sluggish, and factories had no appetite to buy, so the price fell into the customs again, reaching a minimum of 38.4 yuan. However, the Ningbo gang and a manufacturer firmly intended to take delivery, and scattered shorts covered, and the price rose again to 39.9 yuan. In the end, 15,500 dan remained, and the delivery price was averaged at 39.5 yuan over three days. The Ningbo merchants took delivery exclusively. The delivering parties were scattered individual holders. The products were Fire Engine Cotton and Tongzhou Cotton. Spot Yarn and Cotton Consumption is Sluggish

The yarn market remained unchanged, but sales in all directions were quite sluggish. Due to the year-end settlement, the customer gangs stopped, and the customs also closed for three days, making trading even more sluggish. Standard yarn stopped bidding due to the month-end delivery. Only the mainland gangs entered 196 bales, and the Guangdong gangs entered 26 bales. The market situation was similar to the previous day.

The cotton market was still stable. As the overseas cotton market stabilized, the Japanese factory's intention to enter the spot cotton market moved again. The sources were 734 bales of Tong cotton and 659 bales of Yao cotton. The spot cotton prices were as follows:

The Auction of Marked Cotton for May and June Will Continue Next Year as Usual

The Shanghai Yarn and Cotton Exchange has been arguing about the standard of yarn and cotton for a long time. According to market rumors, both yarn and cotton were to be changed. Today at 3 p.m., a meeting of brokers was convened at the exchange's main market to discuss everything. As a result, it was decided that the auction of marked cotton for the May and June terms will start on January 4, 1934, and the standard will remain the same. Everyone unanimously agreed. However, the reform of the cotton yarn standard has not been determined, so the auction will be temporarily suspended until a solution is found.

American Cotton Buyers Active

Yesterday, American cotton initially saw active buying due to strong performance on Wall Street, resulting in a firm and lively market. However, it later retreated as long positions were closed out. Ultimately, spot prices rose by 5 points, while futures rose by 2 to 4 points.

Market quotations: English cotton rose by 5 points, futures by 4 to 6 points. Egyptian cotton spot prices rose by 23 points. Indian cotton initially weakened due to unfavorable news from the India-Japan conference, but later strengthened slightly as short positions were covered. Consequently, Pungole fell by half a rupee, Omra fell by two and a half annas, while White Raw Silk remained unchanged. (Telegraph from the 28th)

Grains

River Rice Prices Remain Stable

(South Shanghai) Only thirty or forty boats arrived from various supplier groups (over five thousand piculs). Among them, the late rice market, although supplies arrived daily, was also scarce. However, due to limited outward channels, stockpiles in the port gradually increased. Moreover, with the Gregorian New Year approaching, there is unlikely to be a large demand. Therefore, its trend lacks the possibility of a turnaround. Observing that sellers show no eagerness to sell off quickly, there will be no sharp downward trend either. This year, only a flat market is expected. Although spot transactions still fluctuate, there are only about six hundred bags in the hands of wholesale merchants and warehouses combined. Consequently, prices remain unaffected. However, special channels have emerged for medium-grade rice recently, with slightly better quality. Merchants have managed to sell off newly arrived stock, leading to a stable market. Short-grain rice is scarce, and good-quality rice is up a few cents. Yin Yuan rice is also slightly tight.

(North Shanghai) Over seventy boats arrived from various places along the river. Due to overcast and rainy weather, few buyers visited the market, resulting in slow sales. Prices for various types of rice, including white japonica, white yuan, yin yuan, early rice, thin rice, Yang Du, and Ke Hsien, remain stable.

Ke Hsien Rice Prices Fluctuate Slightly, Sales Slow

Local Stockpilers Show Interest

Yesterday, the Ke Hsien rice market continued its downward trend from the previous day's weakness. Stockpiles are abundant, sales are sluggish, and market confidence is hard to boost. Yesterday, the price of various types of rice continued to fall by five or six cents, up to nearly ten cents. Following the small price decrease, local merchants began to inquire. Local stockpilers believe that current prices have reached the bottom and there is a need to clear out stock. Holding until the situation stabilizes will likely lead to large sales. Therefore, their mindset has become active. They will likely absorb stock from the market soon. Currently, they are focusing on river rice and factory rice. It is reported that they have already stockpiled tens of thousands of bags. The market can only turn around after local stockpilers inquire about Ke Hsien rice. Yesterday, local merchants and stockpilers completed transactions for 590 bags of Hunan machine oil rice at prices ranging from 7.25 to 7.20 yuan, and 250 bags of machine red rice at prices ranging from 6.85 to 6.80 yuan. Ningbo merchants also took 300 bags of Jiangxi machine late rice at prices ranging from 7.15 to 7.08 yuan. Quanzhou also took 50 bags of Wuhu machine yuan rice at 7.60 yuan, and 180 bags of Wuxi machine yuan rice at 8.18 yuan.

Soybean Prices Show Mixed Trends

Yesterday, lower-grade soybeans continued to rise by three to four cents. Although middle and upper grades were stable, the trend was leaning downward by two cents. Local oil mills and bean curd workshops inquired about purchases and completed transactions for about thirteen to fourteen cartloads. Market sentiment has stabilized slightly. Currently, due to a shortage of railway cars, supplies arriving by train are scarce. As a result, stocks are accumulating in Bengbu and prices are becoming slightly tighter. Supplies arriving by boat are relatively consistent, so the market for Guide soybeans and Dangshan soybeans is still relatively soft.

Sugar Market

Both White and Light Brown Sugar Show Signs of Weakening

Yesterday, the sugar market weakened due to the rise in the Dutch exchange rate and a slight decrease in customs gold. The public association's listed price for 24 coarse granulated white common sugar was 19.40 yuan, down another ten cents from the previous day. Eight/Nine Dutch Red SR mark was listed at 15.75 yuan. The offer for Taikoo sugar was 20.15 yuan, but no transactions were made. Zhenji No. 1 cotton white fell another five cents to 18.50 yuan. Prices for Nos. 2, 3, and 4 remained unchanged. Chaoqing sugar showed little change. A few hundred bags opened yesterday at prices ranging from 12.70 to 12.30 yuan. Jianbang brokers stated that new Diaqing sugar arriving today could be sold at 12.40 yuan, down two cents from the previous listing. The trend still shows signs of weakening.

Dried and Preserved Goods

Shantou Preserved Tangerines Temporarily Out of Stock

Recently, very few Shantou preserved tangerines have arrived, and existing stock is also low. It was reported yesterday that shipments have resumed, but they are temporarily out of stock. The previous listing was 30.50 yuan, and future prices may rise.

Silk and Tea

Foreign Silk Market Remains Weak

New York silk inventories not weak. Since the beginning of winter, imports of Japanese silk into New York have not weakened. According to news from various French firms, New York's silk inventories remain high. Before Christmas, New York City had a total inventory of 70,000 to 80,000 bales of raw silk from China, Japan, Italy, and France. Japanese silk accounted for nearly 70,000 bales, Chinese silk 3,700 to 3,800 bales, and Italian and French silk over 4,000 bales.

Silk waste exports decline. Exports of Chinese silk waste (i.e., silk noil) are declining. In the most recent ten-day period, only 253 dan were declared for export from Shanghai, with no shipments to the Americas. Only 85 dan were shipped to Lyon and Marseille.

Artificial silk sales stagnate as the year-end approaches. As the year-end approaches, credit is extremely tight and sales of artificial silk have completely stagnated. Yesterday, only various ribbon factories on this street had small-volume transactions. The market is quiet. However, the existing stock in the hands of various wholesale merchants is currently being shipped out in batches, making transportation on the Shanghai-Hangzhou railway quite busy.

European and American silk sales remain lifeless. The New York raw silk market has been sluggish recently due to the approaching year-end, making it difficult for prices to hold firm. The sudden rise and fall of Yokohama's Japanese silk prices is purely manipulation by speculators. Real sales in Europe and America are unlikely to turn around. Shanghai's Chinese and foreign silk merchants remain passive, showing no signs of life. Sales of silk fabrics have also stagnated due to the year-end. There is no relevant silk transaction, with nothing noteworthy in the market.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Conversations

Stopgap Policy

— Wei Ba

In the current world, which is full of contradictions, there are many unnecessary things that people know "this road will not work," but they still exist and are carried out. Unemployment relief is one example.

Logically, since heaven has endowed people with two hands, two feet, and a brain, then except for those who do not want to live, everyone has the right to use these tools to obtain the material things they need to survive. No one can deprive anyone else, and there is no reason to deprive them. With the world's capacity, how can "work" be lost? And why is there a need for relief! However, now "unemployment" has become a widespread phenomenon, and "relief" has become an important issue in the domestic policies of various countries.

That "work" leads to "loss" shows that human effort is not fully exerted. But is the lack of human effort due to a surplus in material life, such that labor is no longer needed? The answer is no. The cries of hunger and cold are filling the earth, and even the supposedly wealthiest United States cannot avoid it. It's just that bankers have surplus money in their vaults, and big merchants have surplus goods in their warehouses! Money is hidden on Wall Street, wheat is dumped into the sea, cotton fields are restricted, machines are gathering dust, and the entire society shouts "economic recession"! In this way, we can understand how thirty million people worldwide have lost their jobs!

Once, the Russian novelist Pilnyak traveled to the United States and saw that large factories were closed, machines were gathering dust, goods in warehouses were being gnawed and rotted by rats, and yet there were tens of thousands of gaunt and miserable unemployed workers wandering the streets. He considered it a miracle. Indeed, to someone who has come from another world, this is truly a miracle.

Losing a job certainly entails losing the guarantee of survival. But survival is the last thing every living being wants to maintain. Even chickens and dogs can muster their last strike before death, let alone humans? "Desperation leads to risky behavior," "extremes breed reversals." Smart economists will think of these things. So they have to take out a portion of their profits to serve as relief money, buying a "temporary maintenance of the status quo." At the same time, they can show that this comes from their own "grace," and receive the reputation of "charity" or "generosity," suppressing the crisis. But can doing this patch over this deep-seated unemployment panic, so that the world will be "peaceful and uneventful" from then on? This is something our capitalists don't think about. If they did think about it, they wouldn't be so foolish as to take out thousands upon thousands of dollars every year to do extremely boring relief work, in order to prolong their existence for a short time. Instead, there should be a further step. "The one who tied the bell must untie it." Return work to everyone. But this is not compatible with modern society.

One Aspect of Eastern Civilization – Women's Foot Binding

— Qiong Sheng

Recently, it was reported that foreigners in rural villages around Zhangjiakou took photos of old-fashioned Chinese women with bound feet for malicious propaganda. The government believes this "concerns the national image" and has issued orders throughout the country to strictly prohibit it. Of course, we feel gratified about this matter. Because taking our esteemed country's "three-inch golden lotuses" to be displayed in foreign museums of ethnology for viewing naturally carries a strong sense of insult. Failure to prohibit it would inevitably "concern the national image."

However, Chinese women's foot binding is a product of women being bound by old ethics and teachings. If we want to avoid foreigners displaying them in museums as antiques to be played with, thereby damaging the national image, it seems we should put some effort into the natural foot movement and breaking down the old ethics and teachings. If we want "family scandals" not to be publicized, we should start with eliminating "bad reputations and misdeeds" at the root. The emergence of China's "three-inch golden lotuses" was not like the current "modern" men and women who adopt "Westernization," wearing high-heeled shoes and perming their hair for fashion. Rather, it was like the current trend of society becoming increasingly decadent and dissolute, where women must use their powdered legs and exposed breasts as trademarks to conduct "wholesale and retail auctions," driven by the times and forced by the environment, leading to a temporary craze. Of course, the "golden lotus" had already "swept" the general public, and the adulation of foot-obsessed poets and writers played a significant role in promoting it. Expressions such as "graceful lotus steps" and "elegant and slender" were truly depicted vividly and thoroughly, expressing the desire for all the "talented scholars of the empire" to prostrate themselves at the feet of the "golden lotus." In reality, the main reason was the "men rule the outside, women rule the inside" doctrine. Under the confinement of "inner words do not go out, outer words do not come in" and "locked in deep boudoirs," the feet of some young ladies, famous women, wives, and grandmothers were not used, and naturally became useless. At the same time, because men possessively wanted to keep women chaste and avoid "illicit affairs," binding feet small was a good method. In this sense, "three-inch golden lotuses" did have historical significance in China, and at least made a great contribution to maintaining social customs. If it is said that China still has culture, still has spirits and morals worth preserving, then women's foot binding, which played a significant moral role in the relationship between husband and wife, one of the "five cardinal relationships," although not daring to be ranked alongside "national studies" and "national heritage," is at least one of the national essences!

The worst thing was that foreign battleships and cannons broke through our "closed-door policy," and Western "material civilization" followed, impacting our "land of propriety and righteousness." In social circles, our secluded, virtuous, and tranquil women were required to wear high heels to dance "waltzes" in dance halls and stroll in parks, chatting intimately. Women who did not qualify for the social scene with bound feet were also required to run several miles at six in the morning to work, in order to revitalize industry. Naturally, women with lotus steps were "unable to cope." Therefore, our literary giants and poets, using their exquisite writing skills to describe the "three-inch golden lotuses," which had been the subject of endless praise, had to decline, transforming from a "virtue" into a "bad habit."

Now that the evil custom of women's foot binding is known to all who possess a little new knowledge and are still "modern," especially among young students, who, when they occasionally mention it, inevitably turn up their noses and vomit it out, expressing an unspeakable feeling of hatred and disgust, it can be seen that the natural foot movement seems to have had considerable effect. However, judging from the facts, this is not necessarily so. Many people who cling to "national heritage" and "national essence," and those gentlemen concerned about social customs, seeing the prevalence of dissolute customs, have thus promoted maintaining old morals, respecting Confucianism, and reading the Classic of Filial Piety and Biographies of Women. Some even take the morally rich "Eastern civilization" to resist the purely materialistic "Western civilization." Such a performance is not as straightforward as advocating women's foot binding, praising the "three-inch golden lotus," and wishing that all the talented scholars of the empire would prostrate themselves at the feet of the "golden lotus."

Westerners have a wonderful analogy, saying that if you want to understand the degree of civilization in a country, you can look at the amount of rouge, face powder, and perfume used by women. If you really think that China still has an Eastern civilization to preserve, and still has spirits and morals worth praising, then using this example, we should advise those "Eastern civilization" advocates who hate the world and are jealous of society not to fuss about burying themselves in books to "sort things out." Just conduct a statistical survey on whether the "golden lotuses" are three inches, and whether the "bow shoes" fit "a handful," and you can see the current state of "Eastern civilization."

Not long ago, a European, seeing that Western Christianity was tainted by "material desires" and had lost its original doctrines, did not hesitate to travel across the ocean to China to convert to Buddhism. Buddhism emphasizes purity, inaction, and values spiritual morality, which is also the marrow of "Eastern civilization." This time, the foreigners' taking photos of bound feet in Zhangjiakou may have been with the intention of worshiping the "three-inch golden lotus" of "Eastern civilization"? If my words are correct, not only is there no need to ban it, but the friends of "Eastern civilization" should hold a grand welcome party with "convenience"!

Concerning Women

— Ben

Recently, two friends—Bi is busy getting engaged, Peng is busy pursuing, and when a few people get together, they only talk about women. In these awkward times, it seems that someone has concluded: anyone who talks about love and women

Page 20

is an incompetent good-for-nothing, or at least a declining petty bourgeois. However, we are indeed some "dirt poor" guys, especially Peng; if he doesn't bury himself in doing things he doesn't want to do every day, he may starve at any time.

Originally, we also liked to talk about national affairs, but the times are already "favorable," and it is said that national affairs no longer need us youngsters to yap about. Moreover, for the sake of self-preservation, we are also afraid that the guys next door will hear us and take the opportunity to report us, and we will be arrested. If we are seriously prosecuted, other things don't matter, but the fact that we haven't yet warmed up to the dream of a woman is the most regrettable thing. Bi is most afraid of this, because he has experienced this kind of terror. Even if he is lightly sentenced to three or five years in prison, it is not worth it.

What about talking about the most fashionable "domestic products" or "general construction"? We feel that these things have too little connection with us, and talking about them might not sound very good.

What about talking about romance? We are all some "vulgar and unrefined" crude guys. Forcing ourselves to say a few words would inevitably be a laughingstock, and it would be too disappointing.

So we decided to talk about women. Whenever a few people meet, they only talk about women.

According to the principles of human nature for thousands of years, women are not impossible to talk about. To put it more forcefully, the need for women is almost as urgent as eating, and talking about them is much more stable. Even if we satirize and insult our female compatriots like the French novelist Gauthier, it would only provoke a protest from a certain female writer. As for when we talk about it, no one even bothers to pay attention, isn't that the best way to escape punishment and vent our minds!

The woman Bi found is said to be beautiful in many ways, but there is a large black mole somewhere, which is a flaw, a bit of a "disfigurement" regret. But Bi is madly in love with her and is already engaged. He is afraid that others will notice his lover's black mole, so he tells everyone, "I just love that black mole. When I kiss her, I must first kiss that black mole passionately." Although this philosophy is quite mysterious, it is indeed uniquely meaningful and worth savoring. The female general Peng is pursuing, although her appearance is not bad, we all think her face is too wide and her manner is too martial. But Peng says he loves her wide face and martial manner, almost treating her like an angel, eagerly pursuing her. When it comes to my own sweetheart, I think she is really lovely and really beautiful. If I don't have her, I would rather be single for life. But others tell me to my face that she is not beautiful and not particularly lovely.

In fact, to be fair and objective, each person's woman is only so beautiful and so lovely; however, everyone is very enthusiastic about them, no, very passionately in love with them. In the meantime, compiled into a philosophy, it is: "Any woman one finds for oneself, even if she is not beautiful, she becomes beautiful; even if she is not lovely, she becomes lovely." That is, there is an old saying: "Beauty is in the eye of the beholder," which is indeed true.

Conversely, anything that is passively put together, such as marrying a yellow-faced sister from the countryside, then even if she is beautiful and lovely, she will inevitably become unbeautiful and unlovable, and one will inevitably want to get rid of her. This is the case with several of my brothers, except for one southern friend, who is so honest and immersed in the university of beauties, but always praises his wife who stayed in his hometown to us. This point truly makes us worship him wholeheartedly.

Finally, although the talk is not very serious, it is the true meaning of love between men and women.

The Crisis of University Students

— Dai Dao

Because of the darkness and chaos of society, university students have no way out. Because university students have no way out, there are quite a few people who discuss the crisis of university students. The most effective are the following two views.

The first is that we have now reached the era of the decline of the intellectual class. Although university students are well-versed in both Chinese and Western knowledge and are very adaptable to trends, their social foundation has collapsed, and simply wearing a square hat is no longer enough to exert their authority. Moreover, old consciousness is still so strong, and they cannot get rid of the habits of the literati of the previous era. In fact, literati today are even worse than literati. Look: in this boiling capitalist society of Shanghai, some small vendors, using their skills, earn three to five yuan a day. As for barbers and tea room waiters, their lives are truly comfortable and prosperous. A university graduate must be able to run, jump, flatter, and boast to find a small position—a clerk in a government office or a teacher in a primary or secondary school—to earn a high salary of thirty yuan a month, and even then, they must rely on peaceful times to avoid "budget cuts" and "discounts." This, of course, is like swallowing bitter medicine. Even if you wear a bachelor's cap and have a belly full of formulas, philosophies, science, art, society will not pay much attention to you. Even if your status is as high as heaven and earth, society will not respect you. The era has designated university students of the intellectual class to embark on the path to death, and there is no way out.

The second is that although university students have high reputations and beautiful appearances, they are mostly "gold and jade on the outside, but rotten cotton on the inside" friends, lacking practical skills. Those who study mathematics and science don't understand Chinese, and can't even write a simple letter. Those who study literature even say that they failed Chinese, and can't even solve a simple algebraic problem with one equation. In short, they only know a little bit about everything. When they are in school, they don't work hard and have no foundation at all. When they leave school, they are so arrogant and think they can do everything. When they actually do it, they realize it's not easy to handle, and they don't humbly seek advice, but insist on doing things their own way. As a result, government offices are afraid of university students and want to keep them away. From then on, university students complain about injustice, but in reality, what injustice is there? It's a nail they should bump against. The university students' own lack of soundness is the fatal wound of all crises.

These two views have their own reasons. Of course, we all quite acknowledge the decline of the intellectual class and the poverty of university students themselves. But this is not yet the core of the crisis of university students, nor is it the only reason why university students today have no way out and only have hidden reefs. So what is the crisis of university students? In short, it is "rising desires." Let's see what the general situation is regarding the current university students' understanding of and demands on life.

No matter how poor they are, even to the point of being worried about tuition fees, their appearance and clothing must be so exquisite, and few can clearly recognize that this has little to do with studying. When it comes to food, they are so picky. The food in the school cafeteria seems to be poisonous, and they must wash their bags and go to restaurants to eat heartily. I have seen many university students who do not go to small restaurants. Even if they only have a few cents left for transportation, they must go to a Western restaurant to feel at ease. As for housing, the school dormitories are too crowded, so it's best to rent their own place outside the school. They would rather travel far every day, saying it's more comfortable to live there. We know that desires are bottomless. They are "already high and still rising," climbing upwards every day. From the first year of university to the fourth year, it is clear that there is a big difference. No one is willing to look back and see how the unfortunate friends following behind are starving and freezing.

When they are in school, desires are already so high, so when they graduate and look for a job, their standards are naturally even higher. They don't do things that are too mechanical and uncomfortable, they don't do things that pay too little, and they don't do things that don't have a good reputation. But their demands on life are getting higher and higher. Clothing, food, housing, and transportation must be comfortable and satisfactory. If their pockets are empty, they might as well borrow from others. Even though third-class trains are so empty, they don't bother to squeeze in and lose their status. It's only comfortable to sit in the first-class car with their legs crossed and their heads tilted.

These things are certainly reflected by the capitalist university education in the evil society of the moment, which bred them. But I think university students should not be comparable to ordinary people. Since they have profound knowledge, they must have a correct understanding. How can they go along with the crowd, becoming a social parrot, instead of transforming society and creating an environment? This is truly the crisis of university students! If university students want a way out, half of it must rely on the entire society turning over, but half of it must also rely on quickly reflecting on themselves, recognizing their own crisis, cleansing their own weaknesses, and standing at the forefront of the era to work hard. I think there is a way out, definitely not as dark as it is now.

Rigid Fly

— Bin Fu

On a Saturday evening, I was quietly writing a letter at my desk alone, when suddenly I don't know how a little insect fell on my pen and stopped there, shaking it but it didn't move, driving it away but it didn't respond. I picked up the pen to take a look, and it turned out to be my beloved, long-lost sesame fly. Ah, long time no see, General Fly, how did you become so haggard? Where are your bright wings of the past? Where is your magnificent buzzing song of the past? Where is your happy and lively appearance of the past? Ah, how did you become so thin! How did you become so stiff!

Although the sesame fly was lying stiffly, its beak was still moving non-stop, sucking the ink on the tip of the pen. General Fly, suck as much as you want. Although I am poor, I won't be stingy with this ink. If the ink is not to your liking, then I still have leftover peanut candy by the bed and a full jar of Western honey in the drawer. If these can restore your former health, I will definitely not be stingy.

So I sent our half-stiff fly general to the candy jar and then to the honey jar. The fly general desperately sucked and desperately licked, and the movement of the beak became more rapid. The fly general, who was about to die, seemed to have a "resurrection" phenomenon. I was very happy, and I secretly prayed and blessed our fly general.

The fly general seemed to be full, but it still reluctantly refused to abandon the sweet pottery jar. General Fly, what's on your mind? Could it be that you are thinking of your wife, Miss Mosquito?

It doesn't matter, you can just fly to pick up Mrs. Mosquito. If honey juice and peanut candy can't satisfy Mrs. Mosquito, then my whole body is still full of blood that hasn't been sucked for a long time. If mine isn't enough, there are more from my younger brothers, younger sisters, older sisters, and older brothers. You can just go and pick them up.

Ah, why don't you move? Don't misunderstand my meaning, I don't have any malicious intent of revenge. Although I suffered from cholera in the summer because I drank your poisonous saliva and almost died, and although your wife, Mrs. Mosquito, spread Malaria bacteria on my body two months ago, causing me to have a fever, I will definitely not argue with General and Mrs. Mosquito about these things. I deeply understand our position, our sweat, our blood should be provided for them to suck, this is our duty!

Um, General Fly, why are you always silent and motionless? Could it be that your companions and Mrs. Mosquito have all died? Are you sad? Ah, then I have no way. We have plenty of blood and sweat that can be provided for you to suck, but there is no way in the world to cure your lovesickness. Probably your doomsday has arrived. Doomsday, how can we use our blood and sweat to save you?

Sure enough, that "last remaining" fly general soon died in the honey jar, and I sighed for it for a while.

At that time, there was a copy of Remarque's All Quiet on the Western Front spread out on the table, and a few words suddenly jumped into my eyes:

"...man himself is also a beast insect, but he will spread a little politeness on it like butter on bread."

So I was at a loss. I fear that our doomsday is not far away either.

Page 21

Page 22

Page 23

I Have Three Parts Like Colman

— Ping Ren

The lights in the theater are still on, and the romance film on the silver screen has not yet been shown; but the faces of the young masters and misses who have come to see the so-called love saint Colman are already slightly flushed, as if they have had a bit of wine. This is the elusive magic power of the five words "love saint Colman".

"If I were Colman, all the women in the theater would love me..." I thought comically. Maybe all the young masters in the theater are thinking the same way? I don't need to hit my own head!

"If all the men in the theater were as lovely as Colman and completely in love with me..." I thought all the misses in the theater were thinking that way to themselves—at least, the beautiful miss sitting on my right shoulder, looking at the expression on her slightly flushed face, looking at the inner emotions expressed on the tips of her eyebrows, I thought she was thinking that way to herself.

I don't know what exactly caused it, but I actually smiled at her.

"You smile really like Colman; really, you watch Colman's movies too much, so you are influenced by him!" Mr. Wang, who came to the movie with me, said jokingly, and the beautiful miss actually smiled at my face.

She was saying to her companion, "There's really a bit of Colman's flavor!"

What? Does a person's demeanor become a kind of flavor in her mouth? "Is Colman sweet or sour?" I said to myself, just to scold people "humorously", saying that I wanted to seduce her is really wronging me.

But I ended up seducing her; she laughed out a soft "gezhi...gezhi" sound, and said to her companion, "He himself doesn't know whether his own flavor is fragrant or stinky!" causing the young woman to laugh loudly.

I was feeling very uncomfortable when the young woman said again: "It's as if we've met him somewhere?"

Damn it! Who has ever met you,—but maybe everyone often watches movies and is familiar with each other's faces, right?

My friend Mr. Wang, he is very smart: "Yes, it was the last movie, when we were also sitting together," he actually said randomly.

"No! It was two months ago when we met at the Great Light Theater watching Norma Shearer's movie; he even picked up a handkerchief for her, and later she often said that you have three parts like Colman..." the young woman lowered her head and laughed.

"Don't talk nonsense!" she said casually and laughed again.

Oh! This made me remember that day she asked me if Norma Shearer's eyes were good-looking or not after watching the movie, and I was confused by the surprised emotions, and I didn't answer her but only smiled at her—but I don't know if this smile has three parts like Colman?

"We are very familiar with each other..." I started to say to her, "The two ladies won't mind, right? Let's talk."

"Then, do you think Norma Shearer's eyes are good-looking or not?"

"Hmm—very good-looking, but your eyes are more beautiful and more lively?"

The young woman laughed loudly again, it was simply terrible; she followed with a slight laugh—this goes without saying, was charming.

"Then, do you think Colman is sweet or sour?"

I didn't answer, and the young woman actually leaned over and said in my ear: "You let her taste the flavor, is it fragrant or stinky, and at the same time, you can also taste whether her flavor is sour or sweet?" followed by another laugh, again loudly, causing the guests in the front row to turn their heads.

Ah! This, is too absurd! I thought.

"Don't be prostitutes, right?" Mr. Wang said again, nervously biting my ear.

"Originally, there was a little bit of me like Colman, you are really messing around!"

"No, there are really three parts like him, especially when he smiles." She showed even more closeness to me.

"I'm sorry, I'm very unhappy..."

Saying this, the lights in the theater went out, and the newsreel began to be shown on the silver screen; and her elbow was bumping into my arm again and again, and I hurriedly switched seats with Mr. Wang.

She laughed loudly from her nose, which made my mind tremble.

Novel

Shanghai (31)

— Zhang Lao San

(44) Trailing a Tail

This March, congratulations on my appointment as editor of the "Gong Hua" supplement to the Shanghai Gazette. The meaning of "Gong Hua" was to say some rigid and unyielding words, and initially, it caught a few people to operate on; however, an unfortunate event occurred in the newspaper office. For the sake of the boss's future and one's own rice bowl, it was no longer possible to continue the decapitation work. So, learning a fashionable term, "transformation," "National affairs? Who cares!" "Don't talk about national affairs, just talk about romance," it was at this time that I was accused of touching a woman's behind. In fact, I have absolutely no idea whether a woman's behind is round or square. Although in the Shanghai summer, with the gentle breeze blowing, under the chiffon cheongsam as thin as cicada wings, one can "get a glimpse," ultimately, because "the body is confined within the clothes," one cannot "see the whole picture."

"Shanghai"—originally named Spring in Shanghai—was also being written down bit by bit at this time, preparing to continue the unfinished "Poetry Outline." However, the fate of the poor is ultimately unkind. "Shanghai" was not finished because I was dismissed due to the chaotic period in the newspaper office. However, these written-down "scabby-headed sons" always hoped to be turned into some money. So, I tell the truth, I don't hide anything. Writing articles is simply for the sake of a few coins; the quality of the work is up to oneself but not really cared about. However, my ideal is to write a certain character into a certain type, and this bit of freedom is still held under this broken pen. As for ideology and the way out, etc., I can't manage that much. Perhaps I will ask my friend (borrowing the name) Mr. Ling He for advice on this and then try to cheat a few more coins.

"Shanghai" is finished. For the first half, I slightly revised the old drafts. The second half was scribbled down daily in the broadcasting studio. Furthermore, because the end of the year was approaching, it was hastily concluded. There were countless loopholes and flaws (the issue of technique is simply out of the question). I hope that friends who want to grab people for surgery will be lenient in their writing. "Shanghai" is finished. Apart from the fact that I leave one copy of this publication for myself every day, "Shanghai" has severed relations with me. Therefore, trailing a tail is for the sake of a letter.

When that letter arrived, Miss Xu Huiquin was playing the role of a "city girl." Fortunately, all the way down, Miss Xu did not become a character that caused people to raise eyebrows. The person who worries about Miss Xu (her husband?) can rest assured. However, I want to say something foolish: If you read a novel and worry about the characters in the novel, that's too much trouble. So, I became smart and thought that the three words "Xu Huiquin" must have caused the problem. However, foolish words are ultimately foolish words. Isn't Xu Bingnan precisely Miss Xu's respected father? Taking a step back, there wouldn't be such a coincidence with the secluded villa outside the world in Xujiahui.

I can't recall a novel I read where, because someone was seeking hidden meanings, the author humorously declared that one shouldn't assume that the "someone" refers to oneself just because someone in the book is written as too despicable; if you think that way, you have already acknowledged yourself as a despicable person. I will use these few words to end my tail. Finished, Shanghai, finished, tail. December 27th, at the New Sound Broadcasting Studio.
